Mudarabah — Profit-Sharing
beginner
6 min
The Definition, Pillar, and Conditions of Mudarabah
Definition of mudarabah with its rukn and shurut

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of mudarabah, identify its linguistic derivation, list its pillar (rukn), and enumerate the four conditions (shurut) for its validity.

Core Idea
Mudarabah is a profit-sharing partnership: one party provides capital, the other provides work, with a known shared profit.

This lesson opens the chapter on mudarabah, a foundational contract in Hanafi commercial law. The author explains the term's linguistic roots, its legal definition, the essential pillar (offer and acceptance), and the necessary conditions for a valid mudarabah. Understanding these elements is crucial for distinguishing mudarabah from other contracts like qirad and qard.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic origin and preferred term
Examine the word 'mudarabah' in Arabic and Persian: derived from ضرب (to travel). Note that the Hanafi school chose this term over the Hijazi 'qirad' to align with Quranic usage. Understand the appropriateness with الصلح (settlement) as both involve a single-sided exchange.
The Quranic verse 73:20 is cited as proof for the term.
2
Extract the legal definition
Find the explicit definition: 'عقد شركة في الربح بمال من أحد وعمل من آخر' (a contract of partnership in profit with capital from one and work from another). Break down its components: contract, partnership, profit, capital, work.
The definition excludes fixed profit and guarantees.
3
Identify the rukn and its expressions
The passage states that the rukn (pillar) is offer and acceptance. Note the specific phrases that constitute a valid offer, such as 'I give you this capital as mudarabah' or 'take this and work with it and the profit is half'. The mudarib must respond with acceptance.
Offer and acceptance are essential; without them the contract is void.
4
List the four conditions (shurut)
The passage enumerates four conditions: (1) capital must be from thaman (currency, gold/silver) and known; (2) the capital must be handed over to the mudarib; (3) the profit must be common (shā’i‘); (4) each party's share of profit must be known. These ensure the contract is free from gharar (uncertainty).
A condition missing renders the contract fasid (voidable) or batil (void).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب المضاربة كتاب المضاربة
[١] قوله : كتاب المضاربة ; وجه مناسبته بالصلح أن المضاربة كالمصالحة من حيث أنها تقتضي وجود البدل من جانب واحد.
فإن قلت : إنَّ الصلح إذا كان عن مال يكون بيعاً، والبيع يقتضي وجوبه المبادلة من الجانبين.
قلنا : لا يلزم المناسبة من كل الوجوه، وقد اعتبرت هاهنا في قسمين من الصلح : أعني الصلح عن إنكار أو سكوت. والمضاربة في اللغة : انبازي كردن دوكس بمال وتن. كذا في «الصراح»، مشتقة من : ضربت في الأرض : سافرت، وفي «السير»: أسرعت ، قال الله : وَآخَرُونَ يَضْرِبُونَ فِي الْأَرْضِ يَبْتَغُونَ مِن فَضْلِ اللهِ ) (١) ، معنى يسافرون في الأرض للتجارة، وسمّي هذا العقد بها ; لأنَّ المضارب يسير في الأرض غالباً لطلب الربح.
وأهل الحجاز يسمون هذا العقد مقارضةً وقراضاً من القرض، وهو القطع، فإن صاحب المال يقطع قدراً من ماله ويُسَلّمه للعامل، وأصحابنا اختاروا لفظ المضاربة ; لموافقة لفظ النص.
وفي الشرع ما ذكره المصنف الله بقوله : هي عقد شركة في الربح بمال من أحدٍ وعمل من آخر.
وركنُها : الإيجاب والقبول ; بأن يقول رب المال : دفعتُ هذا المال إليك مضاربةً أو معاملة، أو خذ هذا المال واعمل به على أنَّ ما رزقه الله تعالى بيننا نصفان، أو نحو ذلك من ألفاظ تثبتُ بها المضاربة، ويقول المضارب : قبلت ونحوه.
وشرطها : كون رأس المال من الأثمان وهو معلوم، وكفت فيه الإشارة، وكونُ رأس المالِ مُسلّماً إلى المضارب، وكون الربح بينهما شائعاً وكون نصيب كل منهما معلوماً، كما سيأتيك تفصيلُه إن شاء الله تعالى.
Book of Mudarabah. Book of Mudarabah. [1] His statement: Book of Mudarabah; the reason for its appropriateness with settlement is that mudarabah is like a compromise in that it requires the existence of compensation from one side. If you say: If the settlement is for property, it is a sale, and a sale necessitates exchange from both sides. We say: Appropriateness is not necessary in all respects, and it has been considered here in two types of settlement: I mean settlement with denial or silence. And mudarabah linguistically: being a partner of two people in property and labor. So in al-Sirah, it is derived from: I struck/darb in the land: I traveled, and in al-Sirr: sped. Allah said: 'And others striking/traveling in the land seeking from the bounty of Allah' (73:20), meaning traveling in the land for trade. And this contract is named thereby because the mudarib travels in the land mostly seeking profit. And the people of Hijaz call this contract muqaradah and qirad from qard, which is cutting, because the owner cuts a portion of his property and hands it over to the worker. And our scholars chose the term mudarabah because it agrees with the wording of the text. And in the Shari'ah, what the author mentioned, he said: It is a contract of partnership in profit with property from one and work from another. And its pillar is offer and acceptance, such that the owner of the property says: I give this property to you as mudarabah or mu'amalah, or take this property and work with it on condition that whatever Allah provides is between us in halves, or similar expressions that establish mudarabah. And the mudarib says: I accept or similar. And its condition: that the capital be from valuable metals (thaman) and known, and pointing suffices in it, and that the capital be handed over to the mudarib, and that the profit be common between them, and that the share of each be known, as will be detailed later if Allah wills.
Source pages p. 345

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on mudarabah, a central contract in Hanafi commercial law. The author first justifies its placement after ṣulḥ by noting that both involve a single-sided exchange: in mudarabah, only the capital provider gives wealth while the worker gives labor, unlike a sale where both sides exchange immediately. The linguistic definition uses Persian ('being a partner of two people in property and labor') and Arabic roots: ضرب (to travel), because the mudarib typically travels for trade. The Qur'anic verse (73:20) is cited as evidence for the term. The author notes that the Hijaz school uses 'qirād' or 'muqārada', but the Hanafis prefer 'mudāraba' to match the Qur'anic usage. The legal definition (shar‘an) is a partnership in profit with capital from one party and work from another. The pillar (rukn) is offer and acceptance, with standard formulations like 'I give you this capital as mudarabah' or 'take this and work with it, and the profit is half-half.' The conditions (shurūṭ) enumerated are: (1) the capital must be from thaman (gold or silver currency) and known; (2) pointing to specific money suffices for knowledge; (3) the capital must be handed over to the mudarib; (4) the profit must be shared (shā’i‘) and each party's share known. The passage concludes with a reference to further details. This is a memorization anchor for the basic framework of mudarabah.

Key Terms
المضاربة (al-muḍāraba): A contract where one party (rabb al-māl) provides capital and the other (muḍārib) works, sharing the profit as agreed.
الربح (al-ribḥ): Profit generated from the mudarabah venture, shared according to the agreed ratio.
رأس المال (ra’s al-māl): The capital invested by the owner, must be in thaman (currency) and known.
الإيجاب والقبول (al-ījāb wa al-qabūl): Offer and acceptance; the rukn of the contract.
الشرط (al-sharṭ): Conditions for validity: capital in currency, known, delivered, profit share common and known.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the rukn (pillar) of mudarabah according to this passage?
A) Capital being from thaman
B) Profit being shared
C) Offer and acceptance
D) Work from the mudarib

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of mudarabah emphasizes capital as thaman, known profit share, and offer/acceptance as its framework.

Mudarabah — Profit-Sharing
beginner
6 min
Definition, Pillars, and Conditions of Mudarabah
Introduces mudarabah: linguistic/legal definition, pillar, and conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of mudarabah, identify its pillar (rukn), and list the conditions required for its validity.

Core Idea
Mudarabah is a partnership in profit with capital from one side and labor from the other, valid only when capital is monetary, known, handed over, and profit shares are specified.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya introduces the book of Mudarabah in Hanafi fiqh. The commentator explains the linguistic origin, the preferred Hanafi terminology (mudarabah over qirāḍ), the legal definition as a profit-sharing partnership, the single pillar of offer and acceptance, and the key conditions for validity. Understanding these foundations is essential for distinguishing mudarabah from other contracts like loans or ordinary partnerships.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic definition
Note that mudarabah derives from 'daraba fi al-ard' (traveling for trade). The Hanafi school prefers this term because it matches Quranic usage.
The Hijazi school uses 'qirāḍ' but the Hanafi text emphasizes the Quranic basis.
2
State the legal definition
The author defines mudarabah as 'a contract of partnership in profit with capital from one party and labor from another.' Examine each element: capital, labor, and shared profit.
3
Identify the pillar (rukn)
The pillar is offer and acceptance – the contractual formula (ījāb and qabūl). Recognize that without this, no mudarabah exists.
Hanafi usul: the rukn is the consent expressed.
4
List the conditions (shurūṭ)
The passage lists: capital must be from monetary items (thaman), capital must be known (ma'lūm), capital must be handed over to the mudarib, profit must be shared in a known proportion and must be common (shā'i').
These are conditions of validity – if any is missing, the contract is void (bāṭil).
5
Distinguish from similar contracts
Mudarabah is not a loan (the worker does not guarantee capital) nor a sale (only one side contributes capital). The profit-sharing nature is key.
This distinction prevents confusion with ribā-based transactions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب المضاربة كتاب المضاربة
[١] قوله : كتاب المضاربة ؛ وجه مناسبته بالصلح أن المضاربة كالمصالحة من حيث أنها تقتضي وجود البدل من جانب واحد.
فإن قلت : إنَّ الصلح إذا كان عن مال يكون بيعاً، والبيع يقتضي وجوبه المبادلة من الجانبين.
قلنا : لا يلزم المناسبة من كل الوجوه، وقد اعتبرت هاهنا في قسمين من الصلح : أعني الصلح عن إنكار أو سكوت. والمضاربة في اللغة : انبازي كردن دوكس بمال وتن. كذا في «الصراح»، مشتقة من : ضربت في الأرض : سافرت، وفي «السير»: أسرعت ، قال الله : وَآخَرُونَ يَضْرِبُونَ فِي الْأَرْضِ يَبْتَغُونَ مِن فَضْلِ اللهِ ) (۱) ، معنى يسافرون في الأرض للتجارة، وسمّي هذا العقد بها ؛ لأنَّ المضارب يسير في الأرض غالباً لطلب الربح.
وأهل الحجاز يسمون هذا العقد مقارضةً وقراضاً من القرض، وهو القطع، : فإن صاحب المال يقطع قدراً من ماله ويُسَلّمه للعامل، وأصحابنا اختاروا لفظ المضاربة ؛ لموافقة لفظ النص.
وفي الشرع ما ذكره المصنف بقوله : هي عقد شركة في الربح بمال من أحد وعمل من آخر.
وركنُها : الإيجاب والقبول ؛ بأن يقول رب المال : دفعتُ هذا المال إليك مضاربةً أو معاملة، أو خذ هذا المال واعمل به على أنَّ ما رزقه الله تعالى بيننا نصفان، أو نحو ذلك من ألفاظ تثبتُ بها المضاربة، ويقول المضارب : قبلت ونحوه.
وشرطها : كون رأس المال من الأثمان وهو معلوم، وكفت فيه الإشارة، وكونُ رأس المالِ مُسلّماً إلى المضارب، وكون الربح بينهما شائعاً وكون نصيب كل منهما معلوماً، كما سيأتيك تفصيلُه إن شاء الله تعالى.
Book of Mudarabah. [1] His statement: 'Book of Mudarabah'; the reason for its appropriateness after [the book of] Sulh is that mudarabah is similar to reconciliation in that it necessitates consideration from one side. If you say: 'Indeed, when Sulh involves wealth, it is a sale, and a sale requires exchange from both sides.' We say: 'The similarity is not required in all respects, and it has been considered here in two types of Sulh: Sulh upon denial or silence.' Mudarabah linguistically: partnership of two persons with capital and effort. Thus in al-Sirah. It is derived from 'daraba fi al-ard' meaning 'he traveled', and in al-Siyar: 'he hastened'. Allah said: 'And others traveling in the land seeking the bounty of Allah' (al-Muzzammil 20), meaning traveling for trade. And this contract is named after it because the mudarib usually travels in search of profit. The people of Hijaz call this contract 'muqaradah' and 'qarad' from qard meaning cutting, because the owner cuts a portion of his wealth and hands it to the worker. Our scholars chose the term 'mudarabah' due to its agreement with the wording of the text. In sacred law, it is what the author stated: 'It is a contract of partnership in profit with capital from one party and labor from another.' Its pillar is offer and acceptance: such as the owner of capital saying: 'I give this capital to you as a mudarabah or mu'amalah, or take this capital and work with it on the condition that whatever Allah provides between us is half and half,' or similar expressions by which mudarabah is established, and the mudarib says 'I accept' and the like. Its condition is that the capital be from monetary items and known, and pointing suffices, and the capital must be handed over to the mudarib, and the profit be shared between them in a known proportion, and the share of each be known, as will come in detail if Allah wills.
Source pages p. 345

Commentary
This passage is a definition and introductory ruling from the commentary on the book of Mudarabah. The author first explains why the book of Mudarabah is placed after the book of Sulh (reconciliation): both involve consideration from one side, similar to the two types of Sulh (upon denial or silence). He then gives the linguistic definition of mudarabah, noting that it derives from traveling (daraba fi al-ard) and is also called muqaradah or qarad in Hijaz. The Hanafi scholars prefer the term mudarabah because it matches the wording of the Quranic text. The legal definition is: a contract of partnership in profit with capital from one party and labor from another. The pillar (rukn) is offer and acceptance, with examples. The conditions include: capital must be from monetary items (thaman), known, handed over to the mudarib, and the profit share must be known and common. These conditions ensure the contract is valid and fair.

Key Terms
مضاربة (muḍārabah): A contract of partnership in profit where one party provides capital and the other provides work.
ركن (rukn): An essential element of the contract; here it is offer and acceptance.
شرط (sharṭ): A condition whose absence invalidates the contract; listed for mudarabah.
ثمان (thaman): Monetary items (gold, silver, or their substitutes); capital must be from this category.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum condition for the capital in mudarabah according to the Hanafi school as stated in the text?
A) It must be gold or silver.
B) It must be from monetary items (thaman) and known.
C) It must be cash only.
D) It must be a specific amount.

Key Takeaway
Mudarabah is a contract of profit-sharing partnership, valid only when capital is monetary, known, handed over, and profit shares are specified.

The Legitimacy of Mudarabah: Quran, Sunnah, and Ijma
A ruling with three proofs for mudarabah's legitimacy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three proofs for the legitimacy of mudarabah and explain the Hanafi position on its permissibility.

Core Idea
Mudarabah is permitted by Quran, Sunnah, and Ijma — a contract rooted in mutual benefit.

In this passage, the author establishes that mudarabah is a valid Islamic contract. He cites three sources: a Quranic verse about traveling for trade, the Prophet's approval of pre-Islamic practice, and a story from Caliph Umar involving the sons of Umar. Together, these proofs form the basis for the Hanafi ruling that mudarabah is mubah (permissible).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The text discusses the contract of mudarabah (also called qirāḍ). The ruling is that it is 'mashrūʿah' (legislated/permissible). In Hanafi fiqh, this means the hukm level is mubah.
The author uses 'وحكمها' to introduce the ruling.
2
Locate the Quranic proof
The author cites the general import of verse 73:20, which mentions 'others striking in the land seeking the bounty of Allah.' This includes travels for trade, whether with one's own or another's capital, thus indicating permission for mudarabah.
The dalil is from the Quran (qat'i al-thubut), but the indication is zanni (general).
3
Analyze the Sunnah proof
The text presents two Sunnah-based proofs: (a) The Prophet confirmed people's existing practice of mudarabah. (b) The specific narration of Abd al-Muttalib's conditions for mudarabah, which the Prophet approved.
The second hadith is mursal (from Ibn Abbas), but the Hanafis accept it as evidence.
4
Analyze the Ijma proof
The story of Umar with Abdullah and Ubaydullah shows the Companions practicing mudarabah. Umar initially objected but later accepted it as qirāḍ, indicating consensus among the Companions.
This is considered an implicit ijma (sukuti).
5
Understand the Hanafi conclusion
Based on these three proofs, the Hanafi school declares mudarabah as a valid contract. It is not obligatory but permissible, with detailed conditions found in other works.
All schools agree on permissibility (muttafaq alayh).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هي عقد شركة في الربح زبدة النهاية لعمدة الرعاية وحكمها : ذكره المصنف بقوله : وهي إيداع...الخ، وهي مشروعة بإطلاقِ الآية المذكورة، فإنَّ سفر الإنسان للتجارة قد يكون بمال نفسه، وقد يكون بمال غيره ؛ ولأن من الناس من هو صاحب المال وهو لا يهتدي إلى التصرف فيه، ومنهم من هو بالعكس، فشرعت المضاربة ؛ لانتظام المصالح. وقد بعث رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم والناس يتعاملون بها فأقرهم رسول الله عليها ، وروى ابن عباس أن عبد المطلب كان إذا دفع مالاً شرط عليه أن لا يسلك به بحراً ، وأن لا ينزل وادياً، ولا يشتري ذات كبد رطب، فإن فعل ذلك ضمن ، فبلغ ذلك رسول الله فاستحسنه ، ذكر هذه الرواية الزيلعي في شرح الكنز. وروى مالك : أنَّ عبد الله وعبيد الله بن عمر خرجا إلى العراق فأعطاهما أبو موسى الأشعري من مال الله على أن يبتاعا منه متاعاً ويبيعاه بالمدينة، ويؤديا رأس المال إلى أمير المؤمنين والربح لهما، فلما قدما المدينة ربحا . فقال عمر : أكل الجيش أسلفه كما أسلفكما ، فقالا : لا ، فقال : ابنا أمير المؤمنين أسلفكما أرباح المال وربحه، فراجعه عبد الله ، وقال : ما ينبغي هذا يا أمير المؤمنين ، لو هلك المال أو نقص لضمناه. فقال له بعض جلسائه لو جعلته قراضاً، فأخذ عمر المال ونصف ربحه وأعطاهما النصف، ذكر هذه الرواية العلامة الشمني، فصارت مشروعةً بالكتاب والسنة والإجماع.
It is a contract of partnership in profit. Cream of the Nihaya for the supporting commentary. And its ruling: The author mentioned it by his statement: 'It is a deposit...etc.' It is legislated by the general import of the mentioned verse, for a person’s travel for trade may be with his own wealth or with another’s; and among people are those who have capital but cannot manage it, and others the opposite, so mudarabah was legislated to organize benefits. The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) sent him, and people were dealing with it, and the Messenger of Allah confirmed them in it. Ibn Abbas narrated that Abd al-Muttalib, when he gave money, stipulated that he not travel by sea, nor descend into a valley, nor buy a living creature with a moist liver; if he did so, he would be liable. This reached the Messenger of Allah and he approved it. Al-Zayla'i mentioned this narration in Sharh al-Kanz. Malik narrated that Abdullah and Ubaydullah, sons of Umar, went to Iraq; Abu Musa al-Ash'ari gave them some of Allah's wealth on condition that they buy goods and sell them in Medina, return the capital to the Commander of the Faithful, and the profit would be theirs. When they came to Medina, they profited. Umar said: 'Did I lend the entire army as I lent you?' They said: 'No.' He said: 'The two sons of the Commander of the Faithful, I lent you the capital and its profit.' Abdullah argued and said: 'This is not proper, O Commander of the Faithful. If the wealth perished or decreased, we would be liable.' Some of his companions said to him: 'Make it a qirāḍ.' So Umar took the capital and half its profit and gave them the other half. Al-Shumunni mentioned this narration. So it became legislated by the Book, the Sunnah, and consensus.
Source pages p. 346

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, establishing the legitimacy of mudarabah. The author gives three proofs: (1) Quranic verse (al-Muzzammil 20), which is taken as a general permission for trading journeys, including those with others' capital. (2) Sunnah: the Prophet (peace be upon him) approved mudarabah as practiced by people, and specifically approved the conditions of Abd al-Muttalib (a narrated precedent). (3) Ijma: the story of Umar with the sons of Abd al-Muttalib (Abdullah and Ubaydullah) shows the Companions practicing mudarabah and Umar eventually accepting it as qirāḍ. The Hanafi school thus considers mudarabah as a valid contract based on these sources.

Key Terms
مشروعة (mashrūʿah): Legislated or valid in Islamic law; used to state that mudarabah is permitted.
إيداع (īdāʿ): Deposit; the author uses it as a comparison for the contract's nature.
قراض (qirāḍ): Another term for mudarabah used by Hijazis; derived from 'cutting' a portion of capital.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the second proof (after the Quran) that the text provides for the legitimacy of mudarabah?
A) The practice of Abd al-Muttalib and the Prophet's approval.
B) The story of Umar and the two sons.
C) Ijma of the scholars.
D) A hadith from Abu Huraira.

Key Takeaway
Mudarabah is a valid contract in Hanafi fiqh, proven by the Quran, the Sunnah of the Prophet, and the consensus of the Companions.

Mudarabah — Profit-Sharing

The Composite Legal Nature of Mudaraba
Defining Mudaraba as a combination of contracts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of Mudaraba and explain its five legal transformations: deposit, agency, partnership, transgression, and bida'ah.

Core Idea
Mudaraba is not a single contract; it transforms across time: deposit, agency, partnership, transgression, and gratuitous agency.

The Hanafi school uniquely defines Mudaraba (qirad) as a composite contract that shifts legal nature depending on the phase. This lesson unpacks that definition from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya, showing how the same relationship can be a deposit, an agency, a partnership, an act of transgression, or a gratuitous commission, each with distinct legal consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the essential elements
Note the two components: capital from owner, work from mudarib. This is the core of the definition.
2
Differentiate profit from output
Understand that 'profit' is custom-defined; this excludes muzara'ah where the produce is called 'output'.
3
Trace the temporal sequence
The contract begins as a deposit (iida'), then becomes agency during work, and partnership upon profit.
4
Recognize the violation trigger
If the mudarib violates conditions, the nature changes to ghasb (usurpation), imposing liability.
5
Understand the bida'ah scenario
If all profit is for the owner, the contract is bida'ah (gratuitous agency).

والمراد بالربح هاهنا ما يسمى ربحاً في العرف ، فلا ينقض التعريف بالمزارعة، إذا كان البذر من قبل صاحب الأرض ؛ لأنَّ الحاصل من الزراعة يسمى في العرف بالخارج لا بالربح ، وإن صدق عليه الربح لغة، ولما كان عقد الشركة في الربح غير مستلزم لوجود الربح ، ، فلا يرد أنه قد لا يوجد الربح وقيد الشركة في الربح؛ للاحتراز عمّا إذا لم يشتركا في الربح، فإن العقد حينئذ يخرج إلى البضاعة أو القرض كما سيأتيك تفصيله، وعن الشركة في رأس المال لا غير، فإنه لا يكون العقد مضاربة أيضاً حينئذ ، وعما إذا شرطا فيها الربح لأحد، فإنّها لا تكون مضاربة كما هو الظاهر.
11 ] قوله : بمال من أحدٍ وعمل من آخر ؛ فالربح يستحق بالمال من أحد الجانبين ، والعمل من الجانب الآخر، ولا مضاربة بدون هذه الشركة، وقد فسر بعضهم بأنها دفعُ المال إلى غيره، ليتصرف فيه، ويكون الربح بينهما على ما شرط.
(٢) قوله : وهي إيداع أوّلاً ؛ يعني إن المضاربة إيداع حكماً في أول أوقاتها، وهو زمان بعد القبض وقبل العمل، فالمضارب يكون أميناً حينئذ، فإنَّه قبض المال بإذن مالكه لا على جهة المبادلة والوثيقة بخلافِ المقبوض على سوم الشراء؛ لأنه مقبوض على جهة المبادلة، وبخلاف المرهون، فإنّه مقبوض على جهة الوثيقة.

وتوكيل عند عمله، وشركةٌ إن ربح ، وغَصْبٌ إن خالف ، وبضاعة إن شرط كلّ الربح للمالك
[١]
وتوكيل عند عمله ، وشركة " إن ربح ، وغَصْبٌ إن خالف، وبضاعة (1) إن شرط كل الربح للمالك (٢)
وحيلة أخرى : وهي أن يقرض جميع المال من المضارب إلا درهماً واحداً ويُسَلِّمه إليه، ثمّ يعقدا شركة العنان على أن يكون رأس المال] المقرض درهماً، ورأسُ مال المستقرض جميع ما استقرضه على أن يعملا جميعاً على أنَّ الربح بينهما ، ثمَّ يعمل فيه المستقرض خاصة، فإن هلك المالُ في يده فالقرض عليه، وإن ربح فالربح
بينهما. انتهى. [١]قوله : وتوكيل عند عمله ؛ يعني وهي توكيل إذا شرع المضارب في العمل فيه ؛ لأن المضارب يعمل لرب المال بأمره ؛ ولهذا يرجعُ بما لحقه من العهدة عليه
كالوكيل. [٢) قوله : وشركة إن ربح ؛ يعني وهي شركة إذا ربح المضارب في ذلك المال ؛ فإنَّ المضارب إذا ربح صار شريكاً في الربح ؛ لحصوله بالمال والعمل.
[٣]قوله : غصب إن خالف ؛ يعني وهي غصب إن خالف المضارب رب المال فيما شرط عليه ؛ لوجودِ التعدي منه على مال غيره، قال الشمني (۳) : وبه قال مالك والشافعي وأحمد الله وأكثر أهل العلم.
وعن علي والحسن والزُّهْرِي : إنه لا ضمان على من شورك في الربح. انتهى.
ويكون الربح في هذه الصورة للمضارب ، لكنه غير طيب عند الطرفين. [٤] قوله : وبضاعة... الخ ؛ كان ينبغي أن يقال : والبضاع؛ إلا أن الاسم قد يستعمل بمعنى المصدر، كالعطاء بمعنى الإعطاء، وكونها بضاعة إن شرط كلّ الرِّبحَ
(۱) الإبضاع: وضع السلعة عند آخر ليبيعها دون أن يأخذ على ذلك أجراً. ينظر: «معجم الفقهاء» (ص۳۹).
(۲) لأن المضارب لما لم يطلب لعمله بدلاً وعمله لا يتقوم إلا بالتسمية كان وكيلاً متبرعاً، وهذا معنى البضاعة، فكأنه نص عليها . ينظر : فتح باب العناية» (٢ : ٥٣٨). (۳) في «كمال الدراية» (ق٥٢٣).
Book of Mudaraba: its definition and rulings. With capital from one person and work from another. It is initially a deposit. Its ruling: It is a deposit first, fundamentally, so the definition is not invalidated by the combination. And what is meant by profit here is what is called profit in custom, so the definition is not invalidated by muzara'ah (sharecropping), if the seed is from the landowner, because the produce from agriculture is called in custom 'output' not 'profit', even if it is called profit linguistically. And since the contract of partnership in profit does not necessitate the existence of profit, it is not objected that profit may not exist. And the restriction 'partnership in profit' is to guard against when they do not share in profit, for then the contract becomes bida'ah or qard as will come in detail, and against partnership in capital only, for then the contract is not mudaraba either, and against when they stipulate profit for one, for then it is not mudaraba as is apparent. His words: 'with capital from one and work from another': so profit is deserved by capital from one side and work from the other, and there is no mudaraba without this partnership. And some have interpreted it as giving wealth to another to transact in it, with profit between them as stipulated. His words: 'It is initially a deposit' means that mudaraba is legally a deposit at its beginning, which is the time after receipt and before work. So the mudarib is a trustee then, because he received the wealth with the owner's permission, not on the basis of exchange or pledge, unlike what is received on the basis of purchase negotiation because it is received on the basis of exchange, and unlike the mortgaged property because it is received on the basis of pledge. Al-Shumni said in Kamal al-Diraya: In Sharh al-Tahawi: The legal device to make the wealth guaranteed upon the mudarib is that the owner gives it as a loan to the mudarib, takes a witness, and hands it over to him, then takes it back from him as mudaraba, then gives it to him to use in work for a specified share of the profit. So if he works and profits, the profit is between them according to the condition, and the capital is taken by the loan. If he does not profit, the capital is taken by the loan. If the wealth perishes, it is upon the borrower, who is the worker. Another device: That the owner lends all the wealth to the mudarib except one dirham, and hands it over to him, then they make a partnership of 'inan (equal partnership) such that the capital of the lender is one dirham, and the capital of the borrower is all that he borrowed, on condition that they both work, and the profit is between them. Then the borrower works in it alone. If the wealth perishes in his hand, it is upon him as a loan. If he profits, the profit is between them. End. So he said: 'And it is agency at his work' means it is agency when the mudarib commences work in it, because the mudarib works for the owner by his command, and therefore he is entitled to indemnity for what he incurs, like an agent. He said: 'And partnership if he profits' means it is partnership if the mudarib profits from that wealth, because when he profits he becomes a partner in the profit due to its attainment by capital and work. He said: 'And usurpation if he violates' means it is usurpation if the mudarib violates the owner regarding what was stipulated, because of the transgression on another's wealth. Al-Shumni said: And Malik, al-Shafi'i, Ahmad, and most scholars hold this. And from 'Ali, al-Hasan, and al-Zuhri: There is no guarantee on one who is made a partner in profit. End. And the profit in this case is for the mudarib, but it is not pleasing to both parties. He said: 'And bida'ah...' etc.; it would have been better to say 'al-bida'ah', but the noun may be used in the sense of the verbal noun, like 'al-ata' in the sense of giving. And it is bida'ah if all the profit is stipulated for the owner.
Source pages p. 347

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya is a critical commentary on the definition of Mudaraba (qirad). The author first states the matn definition: Mudaraba is a contract with capital from one party and work from another, and it is initially a deposit. He clarifies that 'profit' here refers to what is customarily called profit, not the linguistic sense, thus excluding sharecropping (muzara'ah) where the produce is called 'output'. The restriction 'partnership in profit' is crucial: if the parties do not share profit, the contract becomes either a bida'ah (the worker acts voluntarily) or a loan (qard). If they share only in capital, it is not mudaraba. The author then explains each segment: 'with capital from one and work from another' establishes the basis for profit entitlement; 'it is initially a deposit' means that before work begins, the mudarib is a trustee (amin), like an agent. The text then presents two legal devices (hiyal) from Sharh al-Tahawi and others to make the capital guaranteed: either by first giving a loan to the mudarib and then taking it back as mudaraba, or by making a partnership of 'inan with a nominal capital of one dirham. The matn then lists the multiple legal natures of mudaraba: it is agency (wakalah) when the mudarib works, partnership (shirkah) if profit results, usurpation (ghasb) if the mudarib violates conditions (making him a guarantor), and bida'ah if all profit is for the owner. The commentary elaborates each: the mudarib is like an agent in work; becomes a partner upon profit; becomes a guarantor (damin) upon violation because of transgression. The author notes that Malik, al-Shafi'i, Ahmad, and most scholars agree on the guarantee upon violation, while 'Ali, al-Hasan, and al-Zuhri held that no guarantee exists because the worker is a partner in profit. The profit in violation goes to the mudarib but is not halal (tayyib) for him. Finally, the author corrects the term 'bida'ah' (verbal noun) and explains that if all profit is for the owner, the worker is a gratuitous agent (mutabarri'), making it bida'ah.

Key Terms
المضاربة (al-mudarabah): A contract where one party provides capital and the other provides work, with profit shared as stipulated; initially a deposit (iida'), then agency, partnership upon profit, and guarantee upon violation.
إيداع (iida'): Legally a deposit; here it means that at the outset, the mudarib holds the capital as a trustee (amin), not as a guarantor.
وكالة (wakalah): Agency; during work, the mudarib acts as an agent of the owner, entitled to indemnity for expenses.
شركة (shirkah): Partnership; once profit is realized, the mudarib becomes a partner in the profit due to his work and the owner's capital.
غصب (ghasb): Usurpation; if the mudarib violates conditions, his possession becomes akin to usurpation, making him liable for loss.
بضاعة (bida'ah): Commission: the worker sells goods without taking a fee; here if all profit is for owner, the worker is a gratuitous agent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does mudaraba not become a partnership until profit is realized?
A) Because partnership requires capital from both sides.
B) Because the contract expressly says 'if he profits' (شركة إن ربح).
C) Because profit is the fruit of both capital and work.
D) Because without profit the mudarib is only a trustee.

Key Takeaway
Mudaraba's legal nature is dynamic, shifting from trust to agency to partnership to transgression based on actions and conditions.

Mudarabah — Profit-Sharing
intermediate
8 min
The Liability of the Mudarib Upon Violation: A Hanafi-Minority Dispute
Defining Mudaraba as a combination of contracts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi position on mudarib liability upon violation and evaluate the opposing view of early scholars.

Core Idea
Majority: violation creates guarantee; minority: partnership in profit exempts from guarantee.

The passage presents a key disagreement: does a mudarib who violates the owner’s conditions become liable for the capital? The Hanafi school, along with Malik, Shafi'i, and Ahmad, holds yes, because transgression of another's wealth necessitates guarantee. In contrast, 'Ali, al-Hasan, and al-Zuhri held that partnership in profit eliminates liability. This lesson dissects the proofs and practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position
The mudarib becomes a guarantor (damin) upon violation, as it constitutes ghasb (usurpation) on the owner's wealth.
This is the view of the majority of scholars.
2
Locate the opposing view
'Ali ibn Abi Talib, al-Hasan al-Basri, and al-Zuhri held that there is no guarantee because the mudarib is a partner in profit.
Their proof: 'la daman 'ala man shurika fi al-ribh'.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
Transgression on another's wealth requires guarantee by default; violation overrides any partnership.
The Hanafi reasoning stems from the general principle that transgression necessitates daman.
4
Analyze the opposing proof
The minority argues that partnership in profit implies shared risk, so the mudarib should not be singled out for guarantee.
This is based on a saying attributed to 'Ali.
5
Determine the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
If capital is lost after violation, Hanafi: mudarib must compensate; minority: no compensation.
This affects risk allocation in Islamic finance.

He said: 'And partnership if he profits' means it is partnership if the mudarib profits from that wealth, because when he profits he becomes a partner in the profit due to its attainment by capital and work. He said: 'And usurpation if he violates' means it is usurpation if the mudarib violates the owner regarding what was stipulated, because of the transgression on another's wealth. Al-Shumni said: And Malik, al-Shafi'i, Ahmad, and most scholars hold this. And from 'Ali, al-Hasan, and al-Zuhri: There is no guarantee on one who is made a partner in profit. End. And the profit in this case is for the mudarib, but it is not pleasing to both parties. He said: 'And bida'ah...' etc.; it would have been better to say 'al-bida'ah', but the noun may be used in the sense of the verbal noun, like 'al-ata' in the sense of giving. And it is bida'ah if all the profit is stipulated for the owner.
Source pages p. 347

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya is a critical commentary on the definition of Mudaraba (qirad). The author first states the matn definition: Mudaraba is a contract with capital from one party and work from another, and it is initially a deposit. He clarifies that 'profit' here refers to what is customarily called profit, not the linguistic sense, thus excluding sharecropping (muzara'ah) where the produce is called 'output'. The restriction 'partnership in profit' is crucial: if the parties do not share profit, the contract becomes either a bida'ah (the worker acts voluntarily) or a loan (qard). If they share only in capital, it is not mudaraba. The author then explains each segment: 'with capital from one and work from another' establishes the basis for profit entitlement; 'it is initially a deposit' means that before work begins, the mudarib is a trustee (amin), like an agent. The text then presents two legal devices (hiyal) from Sharh al-Tahawi and others to make the capital guaranteed: either by first giving a loan to the mudarib and then taking it back as mudaraba, or by making a partnership of 'inan with a nominal capital of one dirham. The matn then lists the multiple legal natures of mudaraba: it is agency (wakalah) when the mudarib works, partnership (shirkah) if profit results, usurpation (ghasb) if the mudarib violates conditions (making him a guarantor), and bida'ah if all profit is for the owner. The commentary elaborates each: the mudarib is like an agent in work; becomes a partner upon profit; becomes a guarantor (damin) upon violation because of transgression. The author notes that Malik, al-Shafi'i, Ahmad, and most scholars agree on the guarantee upon violation, while 'Ali, al-Hasan, and al-Zuhri held that no guarantee exists because the worker is a partner in profit. The profit in violation goes to the mudarib but is not halal (tayyib) for him. Finally, the author corrects the term 'bida'ah' (verbal noun) and explains that if all profit is for the owner, the worker is a gratuitous agent (mutabarri'), making it bida'ah.

Key Terms
المضاربة (al-mudarabah): A contract where one party provides capital and the other provides work, with profit shared as stipulated; initially a deposit (iida'), then agency, partnership upon profit, and guarantee upon violation.
غصب (ghasb): Usurpation; if the mudarib violates conditions, his possession becomes akin to usurpation, making him liable for loss.
ضمان (daman): Liability or guarantee; the mudarib becomes damin (guarantor) upon violation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, who among the following held that a violating mudarib is not liable?
A) Abu Hanifa
B) Malik
C) Al-Hasan al-Basri
D) Al-Shafi'i

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school, in agreement with the majority, holds that a mudarib who violates conditions becomes a guarantor; the minority view that partnership in profit prevents liability is not accepted.

A Legal Stratagem for Mudarabah: Loan Plus Partnership
Presents a hilah combining loan and partnership

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the steps of the Hanafi legal stratagem (hilah) for mudarabah that combines a loan and a partnership, and identify its permissibility.

Core Idea
A loan combined with partnership allows profit-sharing while protecting capital — a permissible Hanafi hilah.

This passage presents a clever Hanafi legal stratagem (hilah) that enables a capital provider to share in profits while still securing his principal. By using a two-step contract — first a loan of almost all capital, then a partnership — the capital provider achieves the benefits of mudarabah without risking the capital as pure capital. Let's walk through the steps and understand why this is considered permissible in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
State the objective of the hilah
Identify the desired outcome: the capital provider wants to share in profit while keeping his capital protected as a loan rather than as mudarabah capital.
The hilah avoids the risk of capital loss in mudarabah while still allowing profit-sharing.
2
Identify the two contracts used
The hilah uses a loan (qard) for almost all the capital, and then a partnership (shirkat al-inan) with a nominal capital for the lender and the borrowed funds as the borrower's capital.
The loan transfers ownership of the funds to the borrower, making him liable for repayment.
3
Explain how the contracts combine
The lender lends all but one dirham to the borrower. Then they form a partnership where the lender's capital is that one dirham, and the borrower's capital is the entire loan amount. They agree to work together (though the borrower works alone) and share profit.
The partnership allows profit sharing; the loan ensures capital return.
4
Consider the legal effects
If the wealth is lost in the borrower’s hand, it is a loan, so the borrower must repay it. If profit is made, it is shared according to the partnership agreement.
The capital provider never loses his principal; he either gets it back or shares profit.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وحيلة أخرى : وهي أن يقرض جميع المال من المضارب إلا درهماً واحداً ويُسَلِّمه إليه، ثمّ يعقدا شركة العنان على أن يكون رأس المال المقرض درهماً، ورأسُ مال المستقرض جميع ما استقرضه على أن يعملا جميعاً على أنَّ الربح بينهما ، ثمَّ يعمل فيه المستقرض خاصة، فإن هلك المالُ في يده فالقرض عليه، وإن ربح فالربح بينهما. انتهى.
Another stratagem: That he lends all the wealth to the mudarib except one dirham and hands it over to him. Then they enter into a contract of shirkat al-inan such that the capital of the lender is one dirham, and the capital of the borrower is all that he borrowed, on the condition that both work together and the profit is between them. Then the borrower works with it exclusively. If the wealth is lost in his hand, the loan is upon him; if profit is made, the profit is between them. End.
Source pages p. 348

Commentary
This passage presents a Hanafi legal stratagem (hilah) for a mudarabah arrangement where the capital provider wants to guarantee profit-sharing and also protect his capital. The method involves two steps: first, the capital provider (rabb al-mal) gives a loan (qard) of almost all the capital to the mudarib, retaining only one dirham. Second, they form a shirkat al-inan (equal partnership) where the capital provider's capital is that one dirham, and the mudarib's capital is the full loan amount he just received. They agree to work together with profit sharing. In practice, the mudarib works alone. If the capital is lost, it is a loan, so the mudarib must repay it. If profit is made, it is shared according to the partnership. This hilah ensures the capital provider shares in profit while maintaining a claim on the principal via the loan. The text ends with 'an-intaha' indicating the end of this topic.

Key Terms
مضاربة (muḍārabah): A partnership in profit where one party provides capital and the other provides work.
شركة العنان (shirkat al-ʿinān): An equal partnership where both partners contribute capital and work, and profit is shared as agreed.
قرض (qarḍ): A loan contract where the lender gives an asset to the borrower to be repaid in kind.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits a hilah that combines a loan and a partnership to allow profit-sharing while protecting the capital provider's principal.

The Six Legal Forms of Mudarabah
Commentary explaining six legal transformations of mudarabah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the six legal forms a mudarabah contract can transform into and explain the condition that triggers each transformation.

Core Idea
Mudarabah is not fixed; it transforms into agency, partnership, usurpation, consignment, loan, or invalid hire depending on conditions.

This passage from ‘Umdat al-Ri‘ayah explains that a mudarabah contract is dynamic. Depending on the mudarib's actions, the profit-sharing arrangement, or the contract's validity, it assumes a different legal character. Understanding these transformations is essential for determining the rights and liabilities of both parties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the six forms
List the six contractual forms that a mudarabah can transform into: agency (wakalah), partnership (shirkah), usurpation (ghasb), consignment (biḍāʿah), loan (qard), and invalid hire (ijārah fāsidah).
2
Match each form to its trigger condition
For each form, identify the condition that causes the transformation: start of work → agency; profit realized → partnership; violation of conditions → usurpation; all profit to owner → consignment; all profit to mudarib → loan; invalid mudarabah → invalid hire.
3
Analyze the ghasb liability dispute
Note that when the mudarib violates conditions, the Hanafi school (with Malik, Shafi‘i, Ahmad) holds him liable (daman) for the capital, while a minority (Ali, Hasan, Zuhri) exempt him due to profit partnership.
This is a thamarah al-khilaf: practical difference in court rulings.
4
Understand the qard and bidha‘ah logic
For qard: if all profit goes to mudarib, he must own the capital, so it becomes a loan. For bidha‘ah: if all profit goes to owner, the mudarib works gratis, making it a consignment.
The commentary notes this is 'by way of predominance' (taghlib) due to the contract's original partnership nature.
5
Reflect on the author's caution about terminology
The author acknowledges that calling mudarabah a loan or consignment is loose usage, but is justified because the dominant feature (profit sharing) gives way to the specific condition.
This shows Hanafi flexibility in classifying mixed contracts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتوكيل عند عمله، وشركة إن ربح، وغصب إن خالف، وبضاعة إن شرط كل الربح للمالك. قوله : وتوكيل عند عمله؛ يعني وهي توكيل إذا شرع المضارب في العمل فيه؛ لأن المضارب يعمل لرب المال بأمره؛ ولهذا يرجعُ بما لحقه من العهدة عليه كالوكيل. قوله : وشركة إن ربح؛ يعني وهي شركة إذا ربح المضارب في ذلك المال؛ فإنَّ المضارب إذا ربح صار شريكاً في الربح؛ لحصوله بالمال والعمل. قوله : غصب إن خالف؛ يعني وهي غصب إن خالف المضارب رب المال فيما شرط عليه؛ لوجودِ التعدي منه على مال غيره، قال الشمني : وبه قال مالك والشافعي وأحمد وأكثر أهل العلم. وعن علي والحسن والزُّهْرِي : إنه لا ضمان على من شورك في الربح. انتهى. قوله : وبضاعة... الخ؛ كان ينبغي أن يقال : والبضاع؛ إلا أن الاسم قد يستعمل بمعنى المصدر، كالعطاء بمعنى الإعطاء، وكونها بضاعة إن شرط كلّ الرِّبحَ للمالك؛ لأنَّ المضارب لما لم يطلب لعمله بدلاً وعمله لا يتقوم إلا بالتسمية كان وكيلاً متبرعاً، وهذا معنى البضاعة، كأنه نص عليها. وقرض إن شرط للمضارب، وإجارة فاسدة إن فسدت. قوله : اعلم أن في هذه العبارة تساهلاً، وهو أن المضاربة إذا كانت عقد شركة في الربح، فكيف تكون بضاعة أو قرضاً، وإنما قال ذلك بطريق التغليب، والحق أن يقول : إن المضاربة إيداع وتوكيل وشركة، وغصب، ودفع المال إلى آخر ليعمل فيه بشرط أن يكون الرِّبحُ للمالك بضاعة، وبشرط أن يكون للعامل قرض، فنظم الدفع المذكور في سِلْكِ المضاربة تغليباً. قوله : وقرض؛ إن شرط للمضارب؛ لأنَّ المضارب لا يستحق الربح كله إلا إذا صار رأس المال ملكاً له؛ لأن الربح فرع المال، فكان تملك المال مقتضي هذا، لكنَّ لفظ المضاربة يقتضي ردّه، فكان قرضاً؛ لاشتماله على المعنيين؛ ولأنَّ القرض أدنى من الهبة؛ لأنه يقطع الحقَّ عن العين دون البدل، والهبة يقطع عنهما، فكان أولى لكونه أقل ضرراً. قوله : وإجارة فاسدة إن فسدت؛ أي المضاربة؛ لأنَّ المضارب عامل لرب المال، وما شرط له كالأجرة على عمله، ومتى فسدت المضاربة ظهر معنى الإجارة.
And it is agency at his work, and partnership if profit, and usurpation if he violates, and bidha'ah if all profit is stipulated for the owner. His saying: 'And it is agency at his work' means it is agency when the mudarib commences work in it, because the mudarib works for the owner by his command; hence he reclaims any liability that befalls him like an agent. His saying: 'And partnership if profit' means it is partnership when the mudarib profits from that capital, because when the mudarib profits, he becomes a partner in the profit, since it is achieved through capital and work. His saying: 'Usurpation if he violates' means it is usurpation if the mudarib violates the owner in what was stipulated, due to the presence of transgression by him on another's property. Al-Shumni said: Malik, al-Shafi'i, Ahmad, and most scholars also said this. From 'Ali, al-Hasan, and al-Zuhri: there is no liability on one who is a partner in profit. End. His saying: 'And bidha'ah...' etc.; it should have been said 'al-bidha'', except that the noun may be used in the sense of the verbal noun, like al-'ata' in the sense of al-i'ta'. And it is bidha'ah if all the profit is stipulated for the owner, because the mudarib did not seek compensation for his work and his work is not valuable except by specification, so he is a gratuitous agent, and that is the meaning of bidha'ah; it is as if he stated it. And it is a loan if stipulated for the mudarib, and an invalid hire if it becomes invalid. His saying: 'Know that there is looseness in this expression,' that is, since mudarabah is a contract of partnership in profit, how can it be bidha'ah or loan? He only said that by way of predominance, and the truth is that it should be said: mudarabah is deposit, agency, partnership, usurpation, and giving capital to another to work with on condition that the profit is for the owner (bidha'ah), and on condition that it is for the worker (loan). So he organized the mentioned payment in the series of mudarabah by predominance. His saying: 'And loan if stipulated for the mudarib' because the mudarib does not deserve all the profit unless the capital becomes his property, since profit is a branch of capital, so ownership of capital necessitates this, but the word mudarabah necessitates its return, so it is a loan because it includes both meanings; and because a loan is lesser than a gift, as it cuts off the right from the substance but not from the substitute, while a gift cuts off from both, so it is more appropriate as it is less harmful. His saying: 'And invalid hire if it becomes invalid' i.e. the mudarabah, because the mudarib is a worker for the owner, and what is stipulated for him is like a wage for his work, and when the mudarabah becomes invalid, the meaning of hire appears.
Source pages p. 348

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary (sharh) explaining that a mudarabah contract can legally transform into six different contractual forms depending on the circumstances and conditions. The author explains each: 1) It is an agency (wakalah) when the mudarib begins working, because he acts on behalf of the owner. 2) It becomes a partnership (shirkah) when profit is earned, since both capital and work contributed to profit. 3) It becomes usurpation (ghasb) if the mudarib violates the owner's conditions, as he then transgresses on another's property. The text notes that most scholars (Maliki, Shafi'i, Hanbali) agree with this liability, though a minority (Ali, Hasan, Zuhri) say no liability if he is a partner in profit. 4) It is bidha'ah (consignment) if all profit goes to the owner, because the mudarib works voluntarily without wage. 5) It becomes a loan (qard) if all profit is for the mudarib, since he only deserves all profit if the capital becomes his property – a loan transfers ownership. 6) It becomes an invalid hire (ijara fasida) if the mudarabah contract itself is invalid, because the mudarib's work is then analogous to rental. The commentary acknowledges that calling mudarabah a loan or bidha'ah is loose usage (tasahul), done by way of taghlib (predominance of meaning).

Key Terms
مضاربة (muḍārabah): A contract of partnership in profit with capital from one party and work from another.
غصب (ghaṣb): Unlawful taking or use of another's property without permission, implying liability.
بضاعة (biḍāʿah): A consignment where the worker works without profit share, equivalent to gratuitous agency.
إجارة فاسدة (ijārah fāsidah): An invalid hire contract; here it refers to the mudarabah becoming an invalid hire when the mudarabah contract is invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) When the mudarib violates the owner's conditions
B) When all profit is stipulated for the owner
C) When all profit is stipulated for the mudarib
D) When the mudarabah contract is invalid

Key Takeaway
A mudarabah contract is dynamic; its legal character changes into agency, partnership, usurpation, consignment, loan, or invalid hire based on real-world conditions and the parties' stipulations.

Three Transformations of Mudarabah: Bida'a, Qard, and Ijara Fasida
Explaining how mudarabah transforms into bida'a, qard, and ijara fasida when profit conditions are altered.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three transformations of a mudarabah contract when the profit-sharing condition is altered, and state the resulting legal relationship and hukm for each.

Core Idea
A mudarabah becomes a different contract when profit is shifted entirely to one party or the contract becomes corrupt.

In a standard mudarabah, profit is shared between the owner (rabb al-mal) and the worker (mudarib). But what happens if the parties stipulate that all profit goes to only one of them? The Hanafi school teaches that the contract transforms into a different legal relationship: a deposit (bida'a), a loan (qard), or a corrupt lease (ijara fasida). This lesson unpacks these transformations and the reasoning behind them.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the normal mudarabah structure
Mudarabah is a partnership in profit: the owner provides capital, the worker provides labor, and profit is shared according to the agreed ratio.
Loss is borne by the owner unless the worker is negligent.
2
Analyze the condition 'all profit for the owner'
If it is stipulated that all profit belongs to the capital owner, the worker receives no compensation beyond his labor. This eliminates the partnership element and the contract becomes a bida'a (deposit), where the worker is a gratuitous agent.
The worker is a wakil mutabarri' (gratuitous agent).
3
Analyze the condition 'all profit for the worker'
If all profit goes to the worker, the capital effectively becomes the worker's property because profit follows ownership. The contract becomes a qard (loan); the owner only gets back the principal.
The worker owns the capital and all its profits.
4
Analyze the effect of a corrupt condition
If the mudarabah contract becomes fasid (corrupt) due to a defect, the worker is still entitled to compensation for his labor. The contract then transforms into an ijara fasida (corrupt lease), and the worker receives ujrat al-mithl (fair wage).
Ijara fasida is invalid but the worker still gets fair compensation.
5
Understand the taghlib (predominance) in terminology
The commentator notes that the matn used lenient language by still calling these cases 'mudarabah' by way of predominance. In reality, they are separate contracts, but they arise from a mudarabah framework.
Taghlib is a rhetorical device; the correct legal classification is as distinct contracts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Book of Mudarabah: its definition and rulings. And a loan if it is stipulated for the mudarib, and a corrupt lease if it becomes corrupt. [1] "And a loan if it is stipulated for the mudarib". So leniency occurred in the expression. It may be said: The meaning is that if after a partnership contract on the basis of mudarabah, it is stipulated that all profit is for the owner, the mudarabah becomes invalid and becomes an ibda' (deposit); and if all profit is stipulated for the mudarib, it becomes a loan." [Footnote 3] "He said: And a corrupt lease if it becomes corrupt; i.e. the mudarabah; because the mudarib is a worker for the owner of capital, and what is stipulated for him is like a wage for his work. Whenever the mudarabah becomes corrupt, the meaning of lease appears."
Source pages p. 349

Commentary
This passage from the commentary (sharh) on the matn of Al-Hidayah explains the transformation of a mudarabah contract into different legal relationships when the profit-sharing condition is changed. The author identifies three possibilities: (1) If all profit is stipulated for the capital owner, the contract becomes a bida'a (deposit) – the worker acts as a gratuitous agent (wakil mutabarri’). (2) If all profit is stipulated for the mudarib (worker), the contract becomes a qard (loan) – the capital is deemed to become the property of the worker, and the profit follows ownership. (3) If the mudarabah is fasid (corrupt) due to some defect, it becomes an ijara fasida (corrupt lease) – the worker is entitled to ujrat al-mithl (fair wage) instead of profit. The commentary notes that the author of the matn used a lenient expression (tasahul) by calling these cases "mudarabah" by way of predominance (taghlib), since they deviate from the standard partnership in profit. The footnotes further elaborate: a loan is chosen over a gift because it is less severe in cutting rights. The correct understanding is that these are not truly mudarabah but different contracts that arise when the profit-sharing condition is altered.

Key Terms
بضاعة (biḍāʿah): A deposit of capital where the worker acts without any entitlement to profit, being a gratuitous agent.
قرض (qarḍ): A loan where the capital becomes the property of the borrower, and all profit belongs to him; the lender only gets back the principal.
إجارة فاسدة (ijārah fāsidah): A corrupt lease where the worker is entitled to ujrat al-mithl (fair wage) instead of profit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if all profit is stipulated for the capital owner in a mudarabah, what does the contract become?
A) Qard (loan)
B) Bida'a (deposit)
C) Ijara fasida (corrupt lease)
D) True mudarabah

Key Takeaway
Changing the profit condition in mudarabah transforms the contract into a different legal relationship – bida'a, qard, or ijara fasida – not a modified mudarabah.

Worker's Wage in Corrupt Mudarabah: Abu Yusuf vs. Muhammad
Intra-Hanafi dispute on ujrat al-mithl cap in corrupt mudarabah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state and explain the positions of Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad regarding the cap on ujrat al-mithl in a corrupt mudarabah, and apply the underlying qiyas reasoning.

Core Idea
In a corrupt mudarabah, the worker gets ujrat al-mithl but Abu Yusuf caps it at the stipulated share; Muhammad does not.

When a mudarabah contract is found to be corrupt (fasid), the worker (mudarib) is not entitled to any profit because the contract is invalid. Instead, he receives a fair wage (ujrat al-mithl) for his labor. But should this wage be limited by the profit share originally stipulated? Abu Yusuf says yes; Imam Muhammad says no. This lesson unpacks their respective proofs and the Hanafi tarjih.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling
First, note that the source states clearly: in a corrupt mudarabah, the worker gets no profit (all profit belongs to the capital owner). Instead, he gets ujrat al-mithl for his work, whether profit was made or not.
This base ruling is agreed upon among the Hanafis (except Abu Yusuf's separate view when no profit is made, which is rejected)
2
Locate the dispute
The source then states: 'and it is not increased beyond what was stipulated, contrary to Muhammad.' This tells us that the dispute is about whether the ujrat al-mithl can exceed the profit share mentioned in the contract.
The stipulated share is often a fraction like half the profit.
3
Analyze Muhammad's position
Imam Muhammad argues that the stipulated share is unknown in amount (since profit is uncertain), so it is like a completely unknown wage. In analogy to a corrupt lease with an unknown wage, ujrat al-mithl is due without any cap.
Muhammad's analogy (qiyas) is to a corrupt ijara where the wage was unspecified (e.g., hire of a specific animal for an unspecified wage).
4
Analyze Abu Yusuf's position
Abu Yusuf argues that the stipulated fraction (like half) is known in one respect – it is a defined portion – though unknown in absolute amount. Since the worker consented to that portion, he cannot demand more than its value when the contract is corrupt.
Abu Yusuf treats the stipulated share as a cap, akin to a partially known wage.
5
Apply the tarjih
The commentary sides with Abu Yusuf, indicating that the mufta bihi position is that ujrat al-mithl cannot exceed the value of the stipulated share (i.e., the share is calculated as if the profit were at the typical level).
The thamarah al-khilaf: if the stipulated share was half the profit and the actual ujrat al-mithl is higher, Muhammad gives the higher wage; Abu Yusuf caps at half the actual profit (which might be less if profit is low), but if profit is high, the cap may still be substantial.

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary on the ruling for a corrupt mudarabah. It states three key points: (1) The worker (mudarib) has no right to any profit; all profit belongs to the capital owner. (2) Instead, the worker is entitled to ujrat al-mithl (fair wage) for his work, regardless of whether the business made a profit or not. This is because he did not agree to work for free, and the stipulated share (i.e., a share of profit) is invalid due to the corruption of the contract. (3) However, the fair wage cannot exceed the amount that was stipulated as the worker's profit share. This is the view of Abu Yusuf, who says that the worker consented to that amount (the stipulated share) as his compensation, so he should not get more. Imam Muhammad disagrees; he says the fair wage is obligatory whatever it may be, because the stipulated profit share was uncertain (since it depended on profit). The text then explains the underlying principle: in a corrupt lease (ijara fasida), the worker gets ujrat al-mithl. If the wage was specified and known, it cannot be exceeded. If it was completely unknown (e.g., hire of an unspecified animal), the fair wage is required without cap. If it was partially known (like a share of profit), it is considered unknown in one respect, and Muhammad treats it as unknown (so no cap), while Abu Yusuf treats it as known in that it has an upper limit (the stipulated share), so the fair wage cannot exceed that. The text also records the view of Abu Yusuf that if there is no profit, the worker gets nothing—like in a valid mudarabah. The commentator rebuts this by noting that a corrupt mudarabah is essentially a lease, not a partnership, so the analogy to a valid mudarabah fails.

Key Terms
أجر المثل (ujrat al-mithl): The fair market wage for similar work, determined by custom and equivalent work.
مسمى (musammā): The wage or profit share explicitly stipulated in the contract.
جزء شائع (juz' shā'i'): A common share or fraction, such as one-half or one-quarter.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In a corrupt mudarabah, the worker gets ujrat al-mithl, but Abu Yusuf's view (mufta bihi) caps it at the stipulated share, while Muhammad allows it to exceed.

Compensation in Invalid Mudarabah: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on mudarib compensation in fasid mudarabah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on the mudarib's compensation in a fasid mudarabah and identify the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
Fasid mudarabah becomes a lease; mudarib gets ujr al-mithl, but Abu Hanifa caps it at the agreed share, while Muhammad gives full market wage.

In a valid mudarabah, the mudarib shares profit as agreed. But when the contract is fasid (invalid due to a missing condition), the nature of the relationship changes. This passage explores the intra-Hanafi disagreement on what the mudarib should be paid: a fair wage (ujr al-mithl), capped or uncapped, and whether profit is a prerequisite. Understanding this dispute clarifies how Hanafi law treats invalid contracts that still involve actual work.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal question
What compensation does the mudarib receive in a fasid mudarabah? The answer depends on how we characterize the relationship: partnership or lease?
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and its basis
Abu Hanifa rules that the fasid mudarabah is like a lease (ijarah), so the mudarib gets ujr al-mithl, but not exceeding the stipulated profit share. The mudarib agreed to that cap, so it binds him.
The cap is the maximum; if ujr al-mithl is less, he gets only ujr al-mithl.
3
State Muhammad al-Shaybani's position and its basis
Muhammad argues the stipulated share is unknown (majhul) because it varies with profit, so it cannot serve as a cap. He gives ujr al-mithl without limit.
This would give the mudarib a potentially much higher wage if the business prospers.
4
State Abu Yusuf's position and its basis
Abu Yusuf analogizes to valid mudarabah: if no profit, the mudarib gets nothing. This view is shared by Malik and some Hanbalis.
The Hanafi response rejects the analogy: valid mudarabah is a partnership, fasid becomes a lease.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and thamarah al-khilaf
The relied-upon position is Abu Hanifa's cap. The practical difference (thamarah) appears when profit is large: Muhammad would give a very high wage, while Abu Hanifa limits it to the agreed share.
When profit is small, the cap may be above ujr al-mithl, so the cap has no effect.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

So he has no profit according to him, rather the wage of his work, whether profit or not, and it is not increased beyond what was stipulated, contrary to Muhammad. So the obligation for the mudarib therein is the fair wage like in a invalid lease, and it is the compensation for his work; because he does not deserve the named share due to lack of validity, and he did not agree to work for free, so the fair wage is obligatory. Source pages p. 350

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the compensation of the mudarib in a fasid (invalid) mudarabah. The author explains that according to Abu Hanifa, the mudarib receives no share of profit (all profit goes to the capital owner), but instead receives the fair wage (ujr al-mithl) for his work, whether there was profit or not, and this wage is capped at the profit share originally stipulated. Muhammad al-Shaybani disagrees, holding that the mudarib is entitled to the fair wage regardless of the stipulated amount, even if it exceeds it. Abu Yusuf holds that if there was no profit, the mudarib gets nothing. The text also notes that al-Shafi'i and Ahmad agree with Abu Hanifa's basic position, while Malik and some Hanbalis agree with Abu Yusuf. The Hanafi response argues that the analogy with a valid mudarabah fails because a valid mudarabah is a partnership (shirkah), while a fasid mudarabah becomes a lease (ijarah) due to the invalidity, thus wage rules apply. The principle derived is that in a lease where the wage is partially known and partially unknown (like a share of profit), there is a disagreement: Muhammad treats it as unknown (ujr al-mithl without cap), while Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf treat it as known to the extent of the cap, hence the wage cannot exceed the stipulated share.

Key Terms
المضاربة الفاسدة (al-mudarabah al-fasidah): An invalid mudarabah contract that fails to meet a condition of validity (e.g., capital not specified) but still produces some legal effects.
أجر المثل (ujr al-mithl): The fair market wage for similar work, determined by what workers of comparable skill receive for similar tasks.
ربح (ribh): Profit generated from the mudarabah capital, which in a valid contract is shared between the capital owner and the mudarib as agreed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is the maximum the mudarib can receive as ujr al-mithl in a fasid mudarabah?
A) Any amount determined by the market
B) The amount of profit stipulated in the contract
C) Nothing if there is no profit
D) Half of the profit

Key Takeaway
In a fasid mudarabah, the mudarib is entitled to ujr al-mithl, but Abu Hanifa's ruling (the mufta bihi) caps it at the stipulated profit share to respect the parties' agreement.

Mudarib's Non-Liability in Invalid Mudarabah
Ruling and reasoning on mudarib's non-liability in fasid mudarabah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that the mudarib is not liable for capital loss in a fasid mudarabah and explain the reasoning based on his status as a trustee (amin).

Core Idea
In fasid mudarabah, the mudarib remains a trustee and does not guarantee the capital.

This lesson tackles a common misconception: that an invalid contract automatically makes the worker liable. The Hanafi school, however, holds that even in a fasid (invalid) mudarabah, the mudarib is an amīn (trustee) and does not guarantee the capital unless he is negligent. The passage from al-Hidayah explains the basis of this ruling through analogy and consensus.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
What is the hukm regarding the mudarib's liability for capital loss in a fasid mudarabah? The passage states clearly: 'la yadman' (he does not guarantee).
This applies even if the contract is invalid.
2
Understand the basis: amin status
Why is the mudarib not liable? Because he is an amīn (trustee). The capital owner deliberately entrusted the capital with the mudarib for trading, intending him to be a trustee.
Al-Isbijabi affirms this as the most correct view.
3
Follow the analogy to ajīr mushtarak
The mudarib is compared to a common hired worker (ajīr mushtarak). Abu Hanifa holds that the ajīr mushtarak is not liable for loss of the hired object, unlike his two companions.
This analogy anchors the ruling in a broader principle of amāna.
4
Note the claimed consensus
Al-Hindawānī says that all scholars agree that the mudarib is not liable in fasid mudarabah. Even Abu Yūsuf and Muhammad would not guarantee here because the capital is a trust.
The intra-Hanafi ikhtilāf on ajīr mushtarak is not transferred to mudarabah.
5
Apply the ruling in practice
If a mudarabah contract is found to be fasid (e.g., because the profit share was unclear), the mudarib does not owe the capital owner anything if the capital is lost accidentally. He only compensates if he was negligent or breached terms.
This protects the mudarib from undue liability.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يضمن المال فيها، ولا تصح إلا بمال تصح فيه الشركة. قوله : ولا يضمن.... الخ ؛ يعني ولا يضمن المضارب المال بالهلاك في الإجارة الفاسدة كما لا يضمنه في المضاربة الصحيحة ؛ لأنه أمين، فلا يكون ضمينا. قال الطحاوي : هذا قول أبي حنيفة ، وهو بناء على اختلافهم في الأجير المشترك إذا تلف المالُ في يده هل يضمن أو لا ؛ لأنَّ هذا العقد بمنزلة الإجارة، والمضارب بمنزلة الأجير المشترك ؛ لأن له أخذ المالِ مضاربة من غير واحد، ولا ضمان على الأجير المشترك عنده خلافاً لهما. وقال أبو جعفر الهندواني : لا يضمن المال في المضاربة الفاسدة عند الكل، وقال الإسبيجابي : وهو الأصح ؛ لأنَّ المال في يد المضارب أمانة، سواء صحت المضاربة أو فسدت ؛ لأنَّ ربَّ المال لما قصد أن يكون المالُ عنده مضاربة قصد أن يكون أميناً، وله ولاية ذلك، ذكره السمني وغيره. قوله : ولا تصح إلا ... الخ ؛ يعني ولا تصح المضاربة إلا بمـال تـصـح فـيه الشركة، وهو أن يكون رأس المالِ دراهم أو دنانير عند الشيخين ، أو فلوساً رائجة عند محمد، حتى أنَّ المضاربة بما سوى هذه الأشياء لا تجوز إجماعاً. والسر فيه : إنَّ المضاربة شركة في الربح ، فلا تصح إلا بما تصح به الشركة، وقال ابن أبي ليلى : تصح المضاربة في المكيل والموزون ؛ لأنها من ذواتِ الأمثال، فتقدير رأس المال بمثل المقبوض ممكن. وقال مالك : إن المضاربة تجوز بالعروض ؛ لكونها متقومة، يستريح عليها بالتجارة عادة، فصارت مثل النقدين فيما هو المقصود بالمضاربة، وتقدير رأس المال ممكن ؛ لكونها متقوّمة ؛ ولهذا تبقى المضاربة عليها، فجواز الابتداء بها أولى. والجواب : إنَّ رسول الله نهى عن ربح ما لم يضمن، والمضاربة بغير النقدين لا يمكن ضمانها بالرد؛ لأن رأس المال لا يتعين فيها، فلا تنعقد.
And he does not guarantee the capital therein, and it is not valid except with capital in which partnership is valid. His statement: 'and he does not guarantee' means the mudarib does not guarantee the capital from destruction in the invalid lease just as he does not guarantee it in the valid mudarabah, because he is a trustee, so he is not a guarantor. Al-Tahawi said: This is the saying of Abu Hanifa, and it is based on their disagreement regarding the common hired worker (ajir mushtarak) if the capital is destroyed in his hand, whether he guarantees it or not; because this contract is like a lease, and the mudarib is like the common hired worker, because he may take capital for mudarabah from more than one person, and there is no liability on the common hired worker according to him, contrary to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). And Abu Ja'far al-Hindawani said: The capital is not guaranteed in fasid mudarabah according to all, and al-Isbijabi said: This is the most correct, because the capital in the mudarib's hand is a trust, whether the mudarabah is valid or invalid; because the capital owner intended that the capital be with him as mudarabah, intending him to be a trustee, and he has authority for that, mentioned by al-Sam'ani and others. His statement: 'and it is not valid except' means the mudarabah is only valid with capital in which partnership is valid, that is, the capital must be dirhams or dinars according to the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), or current coins (fulus ra'ij) according to Muhammad, such that mudarabah with other than these things is not permissible by consensus. The secret therein is: mudarabah is a partnership in profit, so it is not valid except with what partnership is valid with. Ibn Abi Layla said: Mudarabah is valid with measurable and weighable goods because they are of similar types, so estimating the capital by returning the like is possible. And Malik said: Mudarabah is valid with commodities because they are valuable, and one customarily obtains relief through trade with them, so they become like gold and silver in terms of the objective of mudarabah, and estimating the capital is possible because they are valuable; for this reason mudarabah remains upon them, so permitting the initiation with them is more appropriate. The answer: The Messenger of Allah prohibited profit from what is not guaranteed, and mudarabah with other than gold and silver cannot be guaranteed by return because the capital is not specified therein, so it is not concluded.
Source pages p. 351

Commentary
This passage covers two separate but related issues in fasid mudarabah. First, the mudarib does not guarantee the capital (i.e., is not liable for loss), whether the mudarabah is valid or invalid, because he is a trustee (amin). This is the view of Abu Hanifa, analogizing the mudarib to a common hired worker (ajir mushtarak) who also does not guarantee in Abu Hanifa's view. The text notes that al-Hindawani and al-Isbijabi hold that there is consensus that the mudarib is not liable in fasid mudarabah. Second, the capital for mudarabah must be currency (dirhams or dinars) according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, or current coins according to Muhammad, and cannot be commodities, because mudarabah is a partnership in profit, and partnership in profit requires fungible (mithli) capital that can be returned in kind. The text then records a dispute: Ibn Abi Layla allows mudarabah with measurable/weighable goods (mithliyat), and Malik allows it with commodities (uruud). The Hanafi response cites the hadith 'no profit from what is not guaranteed' (which is a principle in mudarabah), arguing that non-currency capital cannot be guaranteed by return because it is not specified ('ayn) in the contract, thus the contract is invalid.

Key Terms
أمين (amin): A trustee who is not liable for loss of the entrusted property unless he is negligent or commits transgression.
الأجير المشترك (al-ajir al-mushtarak): A hired worker who works for multiple people or does not work exclusively for one; his liability for loss is disputed.
ضمان (daman): Liability, guarantee, or responsibility for loss or damage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is the mudarib not liable for capital loss in a fasid mudarabah?
A) Because the contract is void and all obligations are nullified.
B) Because the mudarib is considered a trustee (amīn) and the owner intended him as such.
C) Because the mudarib is a common hired worker and thus automatically not liable.
D) Because the capital owner assumed the risk voluntarily.

Key Takeaway
In fasid mudarabah, the mudarib does not guarantee capital loss because he remains a trustee (amīn) by the owner's intention.
