Mudarib's Purchase of Slave Woman and Paternity Claim
Detailed example of mudarib's liability and capital owner's options in a slave woman paternity claim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a mudarib claims paternity of a child born to a slave woman purchased with mudarabah funds, and explain the condition of solvency in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Paternity claim by mudarib shifts liability for the child's value to the child's labor, not the mudarib's wealth.

This lesson examines a nuanced case in mudarabah involving a mudarib who buys a slave woman with capital, has a child, and claims paternity. The capital owner's options and the mudarib's liability depend on the timing of payment and the solvency condition. The author of 'Umdat al-Ri'aya expands on the ruling from al-Kanz, highlighting an intra-Hanafi difference regarding whether solvency is required for the paternity claim.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and profit share
The mudarib is entitled to half the profit (mudarib bi-l-nisf). The capital owner provides the funds.
2
Trace the sequence of events
The mudarib buys a slave woman for 1000 dirhams (her market value is also 1000). He has intercourse, she gives birth to a child worth 1000. The mudarib claims paternity.
3
Determine the child's value change
Upon paternity claim, the child becomes free-born and his value increases to 1500 dirhams (due to freedom).
4
Understand the capital owner's options
The capital owner may either make the child work for 1250 dirhams (istis'a) or free the child (presumably bearing the loss).
5
Analyze the mudarib's liability for the mother
Only after the capital owner receives the 1000 (presumably the original capital) from the child does the mudarib become liable for half the mother's value (500 dirhams). The solvency condition is disputed: al-Kanz requires solvency, but this author does not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مضارب بالنّصفِ شَرَى بألفها أمةً ، فولدت ولداً مساوياً ألفاً، فادعاء فصارت قيمته ألفاً ونصفه، سعى لرب المال في ألف وربعه ، أو أعتقه [٢] قوله : مضارب بالنصف...الخ ؛ يعني لو اشترى المضارب بالنصف أمةً بألف ، وقيمتها ألف، فوطئها فولدت ولداً يساوي ألفاً، فادَّعى المضارب ذلك الولد، فصارت قيمة الولد ألفاً وخمسمئة ، فرب المال إن شاءَ استسعى ذلك العبد في ألف ومئتين وخمسين درهماً أو أعتقه، فإذا قبض ربُّ المال : أي الألـف مـن ذلـك العـبـد ضـمـنَ المضارب نصف قيمة الأمة. واعلم أنَّ المصنّف له لم يقيد قوله : فادّعاه ؛ بكون المضارب في حال اليسار عند الدعوة، كما قيده به في «الكنز»، وغيره، فإنّه قيد اتفاقي بالنظر إلى الولد والام جميعاً، فإنّه كما لا يضمن قيمة الولد موسراً لا يضمن معسراً ، بل يستسعى رب المال الولد. وأيضاً كما يضمن المضارب نصف قيمة الأم ،موسراً، كذلك يضمن نصف قيمتها
A mudarib with half [profit] bought a slave woman for one thousand, then she gave birth to a child equal to one thousand, so he claimed him, so his value became one thousand five hundred; he works for the capital owner for one thousand two hundred fifty, or he frees him. [2] His statement 'a mudarib with half...' etc.: meaning if the mudarib with half profit buys a slave woman for one thousand, and her value is one thousand, then he has intercourse with her so she gives birth to a child equal to one thousand, and the mudarib claims that child, then the child's value becomes one thousand five hundred: the capital owner, if he wishes, may make that slave work for one thousand two hundred fifty dirhams, or he may free him. So when the capital owner receives the one thousand from that slave, the mudarib becomes liable for half the value of the slave woman. Know that the author did not restrict his statement 'so he claimed him' to the mudarib being in a state of solvency at the time of the claim, as he [the author of al-Kanz] and others restricted it, for it is a coincidental restriction with respect to both the child and the mother, because just as he is not liable for the value of the child if solvent, he is not liable if insolvent; rather the capital owner makes the child work. Also, just as the mudarib is liable for half the value of the mother if solvent, similarly he is liable for half her value.
Source pages p. 365

Commentary
This passage presents a specific case in mudarabah: a mudarib who is entitled to half the profit uses mudarabah funds to buy a slave woman for one thousand dirhams (her market value is also one thousand). He has intercourse with her, and she gives birth to a child worth one thousand dirhams. The mudarib claims paternity of the child (istilhaq), which causes the child's value to increase to one thousand five hundred (since he is now a free-born child of the mudarib, not a slave). The capital owner has two options: either to make the child work to pay off a sum of one thousand two hundred fifty dirhams (alf wa rub', i.e., 1250), or to free the child (perhaps bearing the loss). Once the capital owner receives the one thousand (presumably the original capital or the specified amount) from the child, the mudarib becomes liable to pay half the value of the mother (i.e., 500 dirhams) because he caused depreciation by having intercourse. The author notes that the original text did not restrict the paternity claim to the mudarib being solvent, unlike the author of al-Kanz; here, the mudarib's solvency does not affect the ruling: if insolvent, he is not liable for the child's value either (the child works instead), and he is liable for half the mother's value regardless of solvency.

Key Terms
مضارب بالنصف (mudarib bi-l-nisf): A mudarib who is entitled to half of the profit from the mudarabah.
استسعى (istis'a): To make a slave work to pay off a specified amount; here, the child works for 1250 dirhams.
دعوة (da'wa): Claim of paternity (istilhaq) of a child born to a slave woman.
يسار (yasar): Solvency; whether the mudarib has sufficient wealth to cover liability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the example of the mudarib with half-profit, what is the amount the capital owner can make the child work for?
A) 1000 dirhams
B) 1250 dirhams
C) 1500 dirhams
D) 500 dirhams

Key Takeaway
The mudarib's liability for the mother's half value is contingent on the capital owner receiving payment from the child, not on the mudarib's solvency.

Mudarabah — Profit-Sharing

Mudarib's Claim of a Child: Profit Appearance and Patronage Dispute
Explaining a mudarabah case with mudarib's claim of a child and slave's working for freedom

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the conditions under which a mudarib's claim of parentage becomes effective and contrast the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding patronage and si‘āyah.

Core Idea
A mudarib's claim of a child only takes effect when profit appears; until then, the claim is suspended.

This lesson examines a classic mudarabah scenario involving a slave-girl and her child. The mudarib's claim of the child triggers a complex interplay of ownership, profit appearance, and emancipation. We will unpack the reasoning of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, focusing on how the divisibility of profit (tajazzu al-ribh) affects the outcome.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Scenario and Legal Issue
Read the passage to understand the facts: a mudarib buys a slave-girl for 1000 dirhams, she gives birth to a child worth 1000, and the mudarib claims the child. After the claim, the child's value becomes 1500. The central issue is whether the mudarib's claim is effective and what are the consequences for emancipation and patronage.
The child's value increases only after the claim, but the claim itself is made before any increase is realized.
2
State the Positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn
According to Abu Hanifa, the child must work (si‘āyah) for the capital owner's share (1000 + quarter of profit), and the patronage (walā') is shared between the capital owner and the mudarib. According to the Sahibayn, patronage belongs entirely to the capital owner, and the child works for the capital and the capital owner's share of profit.
The difference stems from their views on whether profit can be divided before the capital is fully recovered.
3
Trace the Dalil of Each Position
Abu Hanifa uses qiyas to a case of joint inheritance where a portion becomes free by operation of law, and he argues that profit only appears when the value exceeds capital. The Sahibayn rely on the principle that profit is not divisible until the capital owner's entire capital is returned.
The text also mentions Zufar's contrary opinion on profit appearance when multiple types of assets are involved.
4
Understand the Key Concept of Profit Appearance
The passage emphasizes that if the mudarabah wealth consists of different items each not exceeding the capital, no profit appears. Profit only emerges when the total value exceeds the capital. Thus, the mudarib's share in the slave-girl and child is contingent on such excess. The claim becomes effective only after profit materializes.
This explains why the claim is not immediately effective; it is conditionally valid pending profit.
5
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf
The practical difference lies in the distribution of patronage and the child's obligation to work. Under Abu Hanifa, the child works only for the capital owner's share; under the Sahibayn, he works for the full capital plus the capital owner's profit share. Additionally, the mudarib's liability for the slave-girl's value differs based on solvency.
The text does not explicitly give a tarjih, but the detailed explanation favors Abu Hanifa's view.

[٢]قوله : وجه ذلك أنّ الدعوة...الخ ؛ توضيحهُ : إِنَّ الدعوة وقعت صحيحة ظاهراً؛ لصدورها عن أهلها في محلها ؛ فإنّه يمكن حملها على أنه ولده من النكاح بأن زوجها منه البائع ثم باعها منه فوطئها، فعلقت منه حملاً لأمره على الصلاح، لكنها لا تنفذ، فإن شرط العتق وهو الملك مفقود ، ولعدم ظهور الربح إذ كل واحد من الجارية وولدها مشغول برأس المال فلا يظهر الربح. ألا ترى أنه إذا هلك أحدهما يأخذ رأس المال من الباقي، ولو كان مجموعها مقابلاً برأس المال يكون منقسماً عليهما فبهلاك أحدهما حينئذ لا يجوز أخذ رأس المال من الباقي ؛ لأن رأس المال في حق الباقي هو حصة الباقي، فلا يظهر الربح : أعنى الزيادة في مقابل رأس المال إلا فيما يزداد قيمته على رأس المال. والسر فيه : أنه تقرّر في موضعِهِ أنَّ مال المضاربة إذا صارت أجناساً مختلفةً كل واحدٍ منها لا يزيد على رأس المال لا يظهر الربح فيه عندنا خلافاً لزفر له ؛ لأن بعضها ليس بأولى من البعض، فإن كان كذلك لم يكن للمضارب نصيب في الأمة ولا في الولد. وإنما يثبت له مجرَّدُ حق التصرف، فلا تنفذ دعوته، فإذا زادت قيمة الولد ، وصارت ألفاً وخمسمئة ظهر الربح فيه في ذلك الوقت، فيملك المضارب منه نصف الزيادة، فنفذت دعوته السابقة فيه لوجودِ شرطها وهو فراش النكاح، إلا أنها لم تنفذ لوجود المانع، وهو عدم الملك، بخلاف ما إذا أعتق الولد ثم ظهرت الزيادة حيث لا ينفذ اعتاقه السابق ؛ لأنَّ الإعتاق إنشاء ، فإذا بطل لعدم الملك لا ينفذ بعده بحدوث الملك.
And the slave works for the value of his share (i.e., the value of the capital owner's share from the slave). (A mudarib with a half share bought a slave-girl for one thousand; she gave birth to a child worth one thousand; he claimed it, so its value became one thousand five hundred. He works for the capital owner in one thousand and a quarter, or he emancipates him. The capital was one thousand dirhams, and the value of that purchased slave at the time of purchase was like that or less, then its value increased above the capital, becoming one thousand five hundred. The mudarib's share became free from him, because he owned part of his relative. So it is necessary that [the slave] be freed proportionally, and he does not guarantee anything of its value to the capital owner, because he had no role in the increase in value; rather, it was freed over him by way of legal ruling due to the increase in value without his choice. So it is like when he inherits him with another: if a woman buys her husband's son, then she dies and leaves this husband and a brother, the husband's share becomes free and he does not guarantee anything to her brother. [1] His statement: 'And the slave works... etc.' because the wealth of the slave is retained with the slave, so he works for it. He becomes free. And know that in this situation, the patronage of that slave is between them according to Imam [Abu Hanifa]; and according to the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad], it is all for the capital owner, and the slave works for the capital and the capital owner's share of the profit. This is based on the difference regarding the divisibility of profit or not. [2] His statement: 'A mudarib with a half share... etc.' means: if the mudarib with a half share buys a slave-girl for one thousand while her value is one thousand, he has intercourse with her, she gives birth to a child worth one thousand, and the mudarib claims that child, then the value of the child becomes one thousand five hundred. Then the capital owner may either make that slave work for one thousand two hundred and fifty dirhams or emancipate him. When the capital owner receives the thousand from that slave, the mudarib guarantees half the value of the slave-girl. And know that the author did not restrict his statement 'he claimed it' by the mudarib being in a state of solvency at the time of the claim, as he restricted it in al-Kanz and others, because the restriction is coincidental with regard to both the child and the mother. For just as he does not guarantee the value of the child while solvent, he does not guarantee while insolvent; rather, the capital owner makes the child work. Also, just as the mudarib guarantees half the value of the mother while solvent, likewise he guarantees half her value. And the capital owner, after receiving his thousand, has the option to hold the claimant liable for half her value. The reason for that: the claim is valid in appearance, being carried on the bed of marriage, but it is not effective due to lack of ownership while insolvent, because it is a guarantee of ownership, so it does not differ with solvency or insolvency, as you will verify if Allah wills. [1] His statement: 'after his receipt' — the condition of his receipt is made so that the slave-girl becomes an umm walad for the mudarib, because she is occupied with the capital. When he receives it from the boy, she becomes free of the capital and becomes all profit, so the mudarib's ownership appears in her, and she becomes his umm walad as we mentioned. [2] His statement: 'The reason for that is that the claim... etc.' Its clarification: The claim occurred valid in appearance because it came from its proper source in its proper place; it is possible to carry it that he is his child from marriage, by the seller marrying her to him then selling her to him, so he had intercourse with her and she became pregnant from him, for ordering matters to be good. But it is not effective, for the condition of emancipation, i.e., ownership, is lacking, and due to the non-appearance of profit, since each of the slave-girl and her child is occupied with the capital, so profit does not appear. Do you not see that if one of them perishes, the capital is taken from the remaining? And if the total were equivalent to the capital divided between them, then upon the perishing of one of them it would not be permissible to take the capital from the remaining, because the capital with respect to the remaining is the share of the remaining. Thus profit — meaning the increase in relation to the capital — only appears in what exceeds its value over the capital. The secret of it: it is established in its place that if the mudarabah wealth becomes different types, each of which does not exceed the capital, profit does not appear in it according to us, contrary to Zufar, because some are not more worthy than others. If that is the case, the mudarib has no share in the slave-girl nor in the child. Rather, he only has the mere right of disposal, so his claim is not effective. When the value of the child increases and becomes one thousand five hundred, profit appears in it at that time, so the mudarib owns half the increase from it; then his previous claim becomes effective in it due to the existence of its condition, i.e., the marriage bed, except that it was not effective due to the existence of the impediment, i.e., lack of ownership. Contrary to if he emancipated the child and then the increase appeared, where his previous emancipation is not effective, because emancipation is a creation; if it becomes void due to lack of ownership, it does not become effective afterwards by the occurrence of ownership.
Source pages p. 366

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a mudarabah case. It presents a scenario: a mudarib with a half share buys a slave-girl for 1000 dirhams, who gives birth to a child worth 1000. The mudarib claims the child as his own, increasing the child's value to 1500. The ruling is that the child must work to earn his freedom from the capital owner's share (1250 dirhams), or the capital owner may emancipate him. The key issue is when the mudarib's claim of parentage (da'wa) is effective. The commentator explains that according to Imam Abu Hanifa, if the slave-girl and child are both occupied with the capital, profit does not appear, so the mudarib does not own any share in them, and his claim is invalid. However, if the child's value increases above the capital (1500), profit appears, and the mudarib then owns half the increase, making his claim effective retroactively? The text discusses Zufar's contrary opinion. The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is whether the mudarib must guarantee anything to the capital owner if the claim is made while insolvent. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is not explicitly stated, but the text seems to favor the view that the claim is valid in appearance but conditional on eventual profit. The passage also addresses the mudarib's liability for the slave-girl's value after receiving the capital from the child.

Key Terms
مضارب (mudārib): The agent managing the mudarabah capital; here, he buys a slave-girl and claims her child.
رب المال (rabb al-māl): The capital owner who provides the funds for mudarabah; he is entitled to his capital and a share of profit.
أم ولد (umm walad): A slave-girl who bears her master's child; upon the master's death, she becomes free.
سعاية (si‘āyah): The slave's effort to earn money to pay for his freedom; he must work for the capital owner's share.
عتق (‘itq): Emancipation of a slave; here, the mudarib's share of the slave becomes free due to increase in value.
ولاء (walā’): Patronage rights between a freed slave and the manumitter; here, it is disputed between Imam and Sahibayn.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The effectiveness of a mudarib's claim of parentage depends on the appearance of profit, and the distribution of patronage (walā') is contested between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn based on their views on the divisibility of profit.

Mudarabah — Profit-Sharing
intermediate
10 min
The Mudarib's Claim of Paternity: Conditions and Effect
Expounds ruling and reasoning for mudarib's paternity claim in mudarabah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a mudarib's claim of paternity is valid in appearance but takes effect only when profit appears, and apply the rule of damān al-tamalluk to determine compensation.

Core Idea
A claim (da‘wah) is a report, perfected later; manumission is an initiation, requiring immediate ownership.

In mudarabah, the mudarib may claim paternity over a child born to a slave-woman purchased with partnership capital. This passage from ‘Umda al-Ri‘āya clarifies the legal mechanics: the claim is presumptively valid due to possible marriage, but it becomes effective only when profit emerges from the mudarabah. The commentator also highlights a key intra-Hanafi dispute with Zufar regarding the definition of profit, and explains why the mudarib's guarantee (damān) is classified as damān al-tamalluk rather than damān al-ifsād.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling and its conditions
The passage states that the mudarib's claim of paternity (da‘wah al-nasab) is valid in appearance (ṣaḥīḥa fī al-ẓāhir) because it can be attributed to a valid marriage. However, it does not take effect until the mudarib gains ownership of the slave-woman, which occurs only when profit appears—i.e., when the total value of the mudarabah property exceeds the capital.
The claim is a khabar (report), not an inshā’ (initiation).
2
Understand the khabar vs. inshā’ distinction
A khabar (like the claim of paternity) reports a past event; it can be valid in form even if the condition (ownership) is absent, and it becomes effective when the condition is later fulfilled. An inshā’ (like manumission) creates a new legal state; it requires the condition to be present at the time of utterance. This is why the mudarib’s earlier claim of paternity takes effect when profit later appears, whereas an earlier manumission would not.
The text explicitly contrasts the two.
3
Analyze when profit appears: the Hanafi position vs. Zufar
Profit (ribḥ) is defined as an increase (ziyāda) over capital. If the mudarabah property consists of multiple distinct goods (a‘yān) each equal to the capital, the majority (Abū Ḥanīfa, Abū Yūsuf, Muḥammad) hold that profit does not appear because no good exceeds the capital. Zufar argues that since the goods are distinct, profit can appear if some goods are worth more than capital individually. The Hanafi response is based on the unity of the mudarabah fund; division is not considered until realization.
The thamarah al-khilāf: under Zufar's view, the mudarib might get a share earlier.
4
Apply the guarantee (damān) rule
Once the claim takes effect and the slave-woman becomes the mudarib’s umm walad, he must pay half her value to the capital owner. This is damān al-tamalluk (guarantee for acquiring ownership), not damān al-ifsād (guarantee for damage). Therefore, it is obligatory regardless of the mudarib’s solvency (mūsir or mu‘sir) and does not require transgression (ta‘addī).
The capital owner may choose to manumit his share of the child or exact istis‘ā’ (earnings).

Source Text

كتاب المضاربة تعريفها وأحكامها

ولرب المال بعد قبض ألفه تضمين المدعى نصف قيمتها ولرب المال بعد قبض" ألفِهِ تضمين المدعي نصفُ قيمتها) ، وجه ذلك " : أن الدعوة صحيحة في الظاهر حملاً على فراش النكاح لكن لم تنفذ لعدم الملك معسراً ؛ لأنه ضمان التملك، فلا يختلف باليسار والإعسار كما تحققه إن شاء الله . [١]قوله : بعد قبضه ؛ وإنما شرط قبضه حتى تصير الأمة أم ولد للمضارب ؛ لأنها مشغولة برأس المال، فإذا قبضه من الغلام فرغت عن رأس المال فصارت كلها ربحاً فيظهر فيها ملك المضارب فصارت أم ولده لما ذكرنا.
[٢]قوله : وجه ذلك أنّ الدعوة...الخ ؛ توضيحهُ : إِنَّ الدعوة وقعت صحيحة ظاهراً؛ لصدورها عن أهلها في محلها ؛ فإنّه يمكن حملها على أنه ولده من النكاح بأن زوجها منه البائع ثم باعها منه فوطئها، فعلقت منه حملاً لأمره على الصلاح، لكنها لا تنفذ، فإن شرط العتق وهو الملك مفقود ، ولعدم ظهور الربح إذ كل واحد من الجارية وولدها مشغول برأس المال فلا يظهر الربح.
ألا ترى أنه إذا هلك أحدهما يأخذ رأس المال من الباقي، ولو كان مجموعها مقابلاً برأس المال يكون منقسماً عليهما فبهلاك أحدهما حينئذ لا يجوز أخذ رأس المال من الباقي ؛ لأن رأس المال في حق الباقي هو حصة الباقي، فلا يظهر الربح : أعنى الزيادة في مقابل رأس المال إلا فيما يزداد قيمته على رأس المال.
والسر فيه : أنه تقرّر في موضعِهِ أنَّ مال المضاربة إذا صارت أجناساً مختلفةً كل واحدٍ منها لا يزيد على رأس المال لا يظهر الربح فيه عندنا خلافاً لزفر له ؛ لأن بعضها ليس بأولى من البعض، فإن كان كذلك لم يكن للمضارب نصيب في الأمة ولا في الولد.
وإنما يثبت له مجرَّدُ حق التصرف، فلا تنفذ دعوته، فإذا زادت قيمة الولد ، وصارت ألفاً وخمسمئة ظهر الربح فيه في ذلك الوقت، فيملك المضارب منه نصف الزيادة، فنفذت دعوته السابقة فيه لوجودِ شرطها وهو فراش النكاح، إلا أنها لم تنفذ لوجود المانع، وهو عدم الملك، بخلاف ما إذا أعتق الولد ثم ظهرت الزيادة حيث لا ينفذ اعتاقه السابق ؛ لأنَّ الإعتاق إنشاء ، فإذا بطل لعدم الملك لا ينفذ بعده بحدوث الملك.

لأنَّ مال المضاربة إذا صارَ أعياناً كلَّ واحدٍ يساوي رأس المال
فإنَّ صحة الإنشاء تعتمد قيام المحلية في الحال، وصحة الإخبار تعتمد احتمال المخبر به في الزمان الماضي، وهاهنا أمكن المخبر ؛ لاحتمال أن يكون على الفراش ؛ لصحة دعوته ظاهراً فينفذ . عند وجود الشرط.
أما الدعوة بالولد فإخبار، فإذا ردّ في حق غيره فهو باق في حق نفسه، فإذا ملك بعد ذلك نفذت دعوته، وصار الولد ابناً له، وعتق بقدر نصيبه منه، وهو ربعه ولم يضمن المضارب حصَّةَ ربِّ المال من الولد ؛ لأنَّ العتق ثبت بالملك والنسب فصارت ة ذات وجهين والملك آخرهما وجوداً فيضاف الحكم وهو العتق إليه ؛ لأن الحكم يضاف إلى الوصف الأخير، ولا صنع للمضارب في الملك ، فلا يجب عليه الضمان ؛ لعدم التعدي ، إذ لا يجب ضمان العتق إلا بالتعدي.
فكان رب المال بالخيار إن شاء أعتق نصيبه من الولد، وإن شاء استسعاه ، فإذا اختار الاستسعاء استسعاه في ألف ومئتين وخمسين ؛ لأنَّ الألف مستحق لـه بـرأس المال، ومائتين وخمسين نصيبه من الربح.
فإذا قبض منه ألف درهم صارَ مستوفياً لرأس ماله فظهر أنّ الأمة كلها ريح ؛ لفراغها عن رأس المال، فكان بينهما نصفين، وينفذ فيها دعوة المضارب، وصارت كلّها أم ولد له، ويجب نصف قيمتها لرب المال موسراً كان أو معسراً ؛ لأنه ضمان التملك.
وهو لا يختلف باليسار والإعسار، ولا يتوقف على التعدي لذلك ؛ ولهذا لو ورث أم ولده مع غيره يتملكها كلّها ، ويجب عليه أن يضمن حصة غيره من قيمتها موسراً كان أو معسراً بخلاف ضمان الإعتاق، فإنّه ضمان الإفساد، فلا يجب عليه بغير تعد إلا على معسر [1] قوله : أعياناً ؛ أي أجناساً مختلفة حقيقة أو حكماً، حتى لو كان أعياناً من جنس واحد كل عين يساوي رأس المال، يظهر الربح كما إذا اشترى فرسين كلُّ واحدٍ منها يساوي ألفاً، ورأس المال ألف كان له ربعُها ، حتى لو وهب رجلٌ وسلّمه إليه صح.
(1) ينظر: «التبيين» (٥ : ٦٢ - ٦٣).
Book of Mudarabah: Its Definition and Rulings

And for the owner of capital, after receiving his thousand, is the guarantee of the claimant of half its value. And for the owner of capital, after receiving his thousand, the guarantee of the claimant of half its value. The explanation of that: The claim is valid in appearance, being construed as based on marriage, but it did not take effect due to lack of ownership. (It is a guarantee of ownership) so it does not differ with wealth or poverty, as you will ascertain if God wills. [1] His statement: 'after his receipt'; the condition for receipt is so that the slave-woman becomes an umm walad for the mudarib; because she is tied to the capital, so when he receives the capital from the child, she is freed from the capital and becomes entirely profit, so the mudarib's ownership appears in her, and she becomes his umm walad as we mentioned.
[2] His statement: 'The explanation of that: the claim...' etc. Its clarification: The claim occurred validly in appearance because it came from its proper person at its proper place; for it can be construed as his child from marriage, such that the seller married her to him then sold her to him, and he had intercourse with her, and she became pregnant, attributing his command to righteousness. But it does not take effect, because the condition of manumission—i.e., ownership—is lacking, and because profit has not appeared, since each of the slave-woman and her child is occupied with the capital, so profit does not appear.
Do you not see that if one of them perishes, he takes the capital from the remaining one? If the total were in exchange for the capital, it would be divided between them, so with the perishing of one, it would not be permissible to take the capital from the remaining one; because the capital with respect to the remaining one is only his share. So profit does not appear—i.e., the increase in exchange for the capital—except in what increases in value over the capital.
And the secret in it: It has been established in its place that if the mudarabah property becomes different types, each of which does not exceed the capital, profit does not appear according to us, contrary to Zufar; because some are not more deserving than others. If that is the case, the mudarib has no share in the slave-woman nor in the child.
Only a mere right of disposal is established for him, so his claim does not take effect. If the value of the child increases and becomes one thousand five hundred, profit appears in it at that time, so the mudarib owns half of the increase; thus his previous claim takes effect in it due to existence of its condition—i.e., the marital bed—but it did not take effect earlier due to the existence of the impediment, i.e., lack of ownership. In contrast to if he manumitted the child and then profit appeared, where his previous manumission does not take effect; because manumission is an initiation, so if it is invalid for lack of ownership, it does not take effect afterward with the advent of ownership.

Because if the mudarabah property becomes distinct properties each equal to the capital...
For the validity of an initiation depends on the existence of the object in the present, while the validity of a statement depends on the possibility of what is reported in the past. And here the report is possible, because it is possible that (the child) is from the marital bed, due to the apparent validity of his claim, so it takes effect when the condition exists.
As for the claim of paternity, it is a report. So if it is rejected with respect to others, it remains with respect to himself. So if he afterwards acquires ownership, his claim takes effect, and the child becomes his son, and (the child) is emancipated to the extent of his share in him—i.e., one quarter—and the mudarib does not guarantee the capital owner's share of the child; because manumission is established by ownership and lineage, so it becomes (a matter) of two aspects, and ownership is the later of the two in existence, so the ruling (manumission) is attributed to it; because the ruling is attributed to the last attribute. And the mudarib has no involvement in the ownership, so guarantee is not obligatory upon him, due to lack of transgression, since guarantee of manumission is only obligatory with transgression.
So the capital owner has the choice: if he wishes, he may manumit his share of the child, and if he wishes, he may compel him to seek gain. So if he chooses compulsion to seek gain, he compels him for one thousand two hundred and fifty; because the thousand is owed to him as capital, and two hundred and fifty is his share of the profit.
So if he receives from him a thousand dirhams, he becomes having fully recovered his capital, and it appears that the slave-woman is entirely profit, because she is freed from the capital. So she is between them in halves, and the mudarib's claim takes effect in her, and she becomes entirely his umm walad, and half her value is obligatory for the capital owner, whether the mudarib is wealthy or poor; because it is a guarantee of ownership.
And it does not differ with wealth or poverty, nor is it dependent on transgression for that reason; and it is for this that if he inherits his umm walad along with others, he takes full ownership of her, and he must guarantee the shares of others from her value, whether he is wealthy or poor, unlike the guarantee of manumission, for it is a guarantee of corruption, and is not obligatory without transgression except upon a poor person. [1] His statement: 'distinct entities' i.e., different types in reality or in ruling, so that if they are distinct entities of one type, each entity equal to the capital, profit appears, as if he bought two horses each worth a thousand, and the capital was a thousand, he has one quarter of them; so that if a man gifted and delivered it to him, it is valid.
Source pages p. 367

Commentary
This passage from 'Umda al-Ri'aya is a commentary on a ruling from Al-Wiqayah regarding a mudarib who claims a child born to a slave-woman purchased with mudarabah capital. The passage type is a ruling with proof (hukm with 'illa).

The core issue: The mudarib's claim of paternity is valid in form (zāhir) because it can be assumed he married her (the slave-woman) from the seller before purchase. However, the claim does not take effect immediately because the mudarib does not yet own the slave-woman—she is still tied to the capital (ra's al-māl). Ownership only appears when profit emerges, i.e., when the total value of the mudarabah property exceeds the capital.

The text explains that if the slave-woman and her child each are worth exactly the capital (or less), no profit is realized in Hanafi law, contrary to Zufar. Thus, the mudarib has no ownership share. If later the child's value increases (e.g., to 1500), profit appears, and the mudarib's prior claim becomes effective, making the child his son. This is because the claim is a report (khabar), not an initiation (insha'); its validity depends on past possibility, not present ownership.

A key distinction: if the mudarib had manumitted the child before profit appeared, the manumission would not become effective later even with profit, because manumission is an initiation requiring present ownership. But paternity claim, being a report, can be perfected when ownership later arises.

Regarding guarantee (damān): If the mudarib's claim takes effect and the slave-woman becomes his umm walad, he must guarantee half her value to the capital owner. This is 'damān al-tamalluk' (guarantee of ownership), not 'damān al-ifsād' (guarantee of corruption). Therefore, it applies regardless of the mudarib's solvency (mūsir or mu‘sir). The capital owner has the option either to manumit his share of the child or to exact earnings (istis‘ā') from him.

Finally, the commentary clarifies that 'a‘yān' (distinct entities) means different types in reality or ruling. If the entities are all of one type but each equals the capital, profit still appears (e.g., two horses each worth 1000 with capital 1000, the mudarib owns a quarter of each).

Key Terms
دعوة (da‘wah): Claim of paternity (إثبات النسب) by a mudarib over a child born to a slave-woman in the mudarabah.
أم ولد (umm walad): A slave-woman who bears a child to her master; here the mudarib's slave-woman becomes umm walad when his claim takes effect, entitling him to her ownership and freeing her upon his death.
ضمان التملك (damān al-tamalluk): A guarantee for acquiring ownership; here the mudarib must pay half value to the capital owner because he takes full ownership of the umm walad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the mudarib's guarantee of half the slave-woman's value not depend on his solvency?
A) Because it is a penalty for transgression
B) Because it is a guarantee of ownership (damān al-tamalluk), not a guarantee of corruption
C) Because the capital owner is always wealthy
D) Because the mudarib is always wealthy

Key Takeaway
The mudarib's claim of paternity is a report that takes effect only when profit appears, and his guarantee is damān al-tamalluk, not dependent on solvency.

Ruling on Mudarib's Claim of Paternity and Its Effects
Expounds the ruling on mudarib's da'wa bi'l-walad and its legal consequences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a mudarib does not guarantee the principal's share of the child and state the principal's options under Hanafi law.

Core Idea
The mudarib's paternity claim frees only his share; no guarantee for the child, but full ownership later triggers daman al-tamalluk.

This passage from a later Hanafi commentary expands on the legal consequences when a mudarib (investment agent) claims paternity of a child born to a slave-girl purchased with mudarabah funds. It clarifies the interplay of ownership, emancipation, and guarantee, distinguishing between the present creation of ownership and the past informational claim of paternity. The mudarib's claim is valid if he later acquires full ownership, but the principal retains a choice regarding his share of the child.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish creation from information
Identify the general rule: ownership creation depends on immediate basis; informational claims depend on past possibility. Recognize that paternity claim is an informational report, and here it is possible because the child could have been conceived on the mudarib's bed.
2
Determine initial effect of paternity claim
Understand that the claim is partially effective: it establishes lineage and emancipates the child to the extent of the mudarib's ownership share (one-fourth in this scenario). The principal's share remains unaffected.
3
Analyze why no guarantee for child's share
Follow the reasoning: emancipation is attributed to ownership and lineage, and since ownership arises later, the ruling is attached to the later cause. The mudarib did not cause the principal's share to be owned, so no transgression and no guarantee for the child.
4
Identify the principal's options
The principal may either free his share of the child or seek compensation (istis'a) from the child for his share. Note the calculation: compensation includes capital and profit.
5
Understand the final guarantee (daman al-tamalluk)
Once the principal's capital is satisfied, the slave-girl becomes all profit and the mudarib's claim makes her his umm walad. He must pay half her value as daman al-tamalluk, regardless of wealth or transgression. Compare to inheriting an umm walad with others.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لأنَّ مال المضاربة إذا صارَ أعياناً كلَّ واحدٍ يساوي رأس المال فإنَّ صحة الإنشاء تعتمد قيام المحلية في الحال، وصحة الإخبار تعتمد احتمال المخبر به في الزمان الماضي، وهاهنا أمكن المخبر ؛ لاحتمال أن يكون على الفراش ؛ لصحة دعوته ظاهراً فينفذ . عند وجود الشرط. أما الدعوة بالولد فإخبار، فإذا ردّ في حق غيره فهو باق في حق نفسه، فإذا ملك بعد ذلك نفذت دعوته، وصار الولد ابناً له، وعتق بقدر نصيبه منه، وهو ربعه ولم يضمن المضارب حصَّةَ ربِّ المال من الولد ؛ لأنَّ العتق ثبت بالملك والنسب فصارت [؟] ذات وجهين والملك آخرهما وجوداً فيضاف الحكم وهو العتق إليه ؛ لأن الحكم يضاف إلى الوصف الأخير، ولا صنع للمضارب في الملك ، فلا يجب عليه الضمان ؛ لعدم التعدي ، إذ لا يجب ضمان العتق إلا بالتعدي. فكان رب المال بالخيار إن شاء أعتق نصيبه من الولد، وإن شاء استسعاه ، فإذا اختار الاستسعاء استسعاه في ألف ومئتين وخمسين ؛ لأنَّ الألف مستحق لـه بـرأس المال، ومائتين وخمسين نصيبه من الربح. فإذا قبض منه ألف درهم صارَ مستوفياً لرأس ماله فظهر أنّ الأمة كلها ربح ؛ لفراغها عن رأس المال، فكان بينهما نصفين، وينفذ فيها دعوة المضارب، وصارت كلّها أم ولد له، ويجب نصف قيمتها لرب المال موسراً كان أو معسراً ؛ لأنه ضمان التملك. وهو لا يختلف باليسار والإعسار، ولا يتوقف على التعدي لذلك ؛ ولهذا لو ورث أم ولده مع غيره يتملكها كلّها ، ويجب عليه أن يضمن حصة غيره من قيمتها موسراً كان أو معسراً بخلاف ضمان الإعتاق، فإنّه ضمان الإفساد، فلا يجب عليه بغير تعد إلا على معسر
Because if the mudarabah property becomes specific goods each equal to the capital, then the validity of creation (of ownership) depends on the existence of the basis immediately, and the validity of information (of claim) depends on the possibility of the informed matter in the past time. Here the information is possible because it is possible that (the child) was on the bed due to the apparent validity of his claim, so it is executed when the condition exists. As for the claim of paternity, it is information. So if it is rejected with respect to someone else's right, it remains valid with respect to his own right. So if he later owns (the child), his claim is executed, and the child becomes his son, and is emancipated to the extent of his share, which is one-fourth. The mudarib does not guarantee the principal's share of the child because emancipation is established by ownership and lineage, so it becomes [؟] having two aspects, and ownership is the later of them in existence, so the ruling, which is emancipation, is attributed to it because the ruling is attributed to the last description. The mudarib has no role in the ownership, so guarantee is not incumbent upon him due to lack of transgression, since guarantee of emancipation is only incumbent due to transgression. So the principal has a choice: if he wishes, he frees his share of the child; if he wishes, he seeks compensation from him. If he chooses compensation, he seeks compensation from him for one thousand two hundred and fifty because the thousand is owed to him as capital, and two hundred and fifty is his share of profit. If he collects one thousand dirhams from him, he becomes satisfied for his capital, so it becomes apparent that the slave-girl is all profit because it is vacated from the capital, so it is half between them, and the mudarib's claim in her is executed, and she becomes all umm walad for him, and half of her value is obligatory for the principal, whether he is wealthy or insolvent, because it is a guarantee of ownership. And it does not differ with wealth or insolvency, and it is not contingent on transgression for that reason. Thus, if he inherits his umm walad along with others, he owns all of her, and he must guarantee the share of others from her value, whether he is wealthy or insolvent, unlike the guarantee of emancipation, for it is a guarantee of corruption, so it is not incumbent without transgression except upon an insolvent.
Source pages p. 368

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the ruling regarding a mudarib (agent in a mudarabah partnership) who claims paternity of a child born to a slave-girl purchased with mudarabah funds. The commentary first addresses a general principle: the validity of creating ownership (in the present) depends on the immediate existence of its basis, while the validity of an informational claim (like paternity, referring to the past) depends on the possibility of the event in the past. In this case, the claim is possible because the child could have been conceived while the mudarib was lawfully with the slave-girl (on the bed), so his claim is valid if conditions are met. Specifically, the claim of paternity is an informational report (ikhbar). If it is rejected in the right of someone else (e.g., the principal), it remains valid in the mudarib's own right. Once the mudarib later acquires full ownership of the slave-girl (through profit), his prior claim becomes effective, lineage is established, and the child becomes his son. However, at the time of the claim, the mudarib only owned a share (one-fourth) of the slave-girl, so only that share of the child is emancipated. The mudarib does not have to compensate the principal for his share of the child because the emancipation (itq) is legally attributed to ownership and lineage together, and since ownership arose later, the ruling (emancipation) is attached to that later cause. The mudarib did not cause the ownership, so he is not a transgressor; guarantee (daman) for emancipation only applies in cases of transgression. The principal has a choice: either free his own share of the child or seek compensation (istis'a) from the child for his share. The compensation amount is 1250 dirhams: 1000 for the principal's capital and 250 as his share of profit. If the principal collects 1000 dirhams from the child, his capital is satisfied, and the slave-girl becomes entirely profit (since she is now free of the capital claim). Consequently, she is owned equally by both parties, and the mudarib's claim becomes fully effective, making her his umm walad (mother of his child). He must then pay half her value to the principal as a guarantee of ownership (daman al-tamalluk), regardless of the principal's financial status or whether the mudarib acted wrongfully. This is analogous to inheriting an umm walad with others: if one inherits her, he owns her entirely but must pay the other heirs their shares of her value, regardless of his own wealth. This contrasts with the guarantee of emancipation, which is a guarantee for spoiling property and is only due if the mudarib acted transgressively, and even then only from an insolvent.

Key Terms
دعوة بالولد (da'wa bi'l-walad): The claim by a man that a child born to a slave-girl he owns (or partially owns) is his offspring.
ضمان التملك (daman al-tamalluk): A guarantee that arises when one acquires ownership of property that belongs partly to another, requiring compensation for the other's share.
عتق (itq): Emancipation of a slave, which in this context occurs proportionally to the mudarib's share of ownership.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the principal's option if the mudarib claims paternity of a child born to the slave-girl?
A) He must free his share of the child immediately.
B) He may choose to free his share or seek compensation (istis'a) from the child.
C) He must sell the child and divide the proceeds.
D) He automatically loses his share to the mudarib.

Key Takeaway
The mudarib's paternity claim is effective retroactively upon full ownership; he owes compensation for the full slave-girl (daman al-tamalluk) but not for the principal's share of the child.

Mudarabah — Profit-Sharing

When Profit Appears in Mudarabah: Mudarib's Paternity Claim
Explains profit realization and paternity claim conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the condition under which profit appears in a mudarabah involving goods, and apply it to determine when a mudarib's claim of paternity is effective.

Core Idea
Profit appears only when total value exceeds capital; without profit, the mudarib has no ownership to support a claim.

In mudarabah, profit is the increase over capital. When the mudarib converts capital into goods, profit is not automatically realized if goods equal capital. This lesson explains when profit appears, and how it enables the mudarib to claim paternity of a child from a slave-girl purchased with mudarabah funds.

Guided Path
1
Identify Capital and Goods
Determine the capital amount and the goods purchased. Note their types (same or different) and individual values.
2
Assess Total Value vs Capital
Compare the total market value of all goods to the capital. Profit appears only if total value exceeds capital.
If goods are of one type and each equals capital, no profit yet because any could represent capital.
3
Check Profit Appearance for Mudarib's Claim
If profit appears, the mudarib acquires partial ownership in the goods, including any offspring. This ownership is necessary for a valid paternity claim (istila').
4
Calculate Payment Upon Profit
Once profit appears, the mudarib must pay the principal's capital and share of profit. Then the child is free in proportion, and the mother becomes umm walad.
Example: mother's value increases to 1500, capital 1000, profit 500. Mudarib owns half profit (250), pays 1250, child free half, mother umm walad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[١] قوله : أعياناً ؛ أي أجناساً مختلفة حقيقة أو حكماً، حتى لو كان أعياناً من جنس واحد كل عين يساوي رأس المال، يظهر الربح كما إذا اشترى فرسين كلُّ واحدٍ منها يساوي ألفاً، ورأس المال ألف كان له ربعُها ، حتى لو وهب رجلٌ وسلّمه إليه صح. لا يظهر الربح، بل كلُّ واحدٍ يصلح أن يكون رأس المال ؛ لأنه يمكن أن يهلَكَ ما سواه، ويبقى واحد فقط، فلا رجحان لأحد لكونه رأس المال، أو ربحاً. ثُمَّ إذا زادت القيمة بعد الدعوة حتى صارَ قيمة الولد ألفاً وخمسمئة ظَهَرَ الربح ، فنفذت الدعوة السابقة، ويثبت النسب ، وعتق الولد لقيام ملكه في البعض أما العبد فعند أبي حنيفة له أجناس مختلفة ؛ لفحش التفاوت في المعاني الباطنة، وعندهما كذلك ، إلا أن يرى القاضي الصلاح في الجميع، أو يتراضوا على ذلك ، فحينئذ يجمع. كذا في «الكفاية». [١] قوله : لا يظهر الربح ؛ فإذا لم يظهر الربح لم يكن للمضارب في الجارية ملك، وبدون الملك لا يثبت الاستيلاء. [٢] قوله : ثم إذا زادت القيمة...الخ ؛ ولو لم تزد قيمة الولد على ألف، وزادت قيمة الأم حتى صارت ألفاً وخمسمئة صارتِ الجارية أم ولد للمضارب، ويضمن لرب المال ألف درهم ومئتين وخمسين درهماً ؛ لأنها لما زادت قيمتها ظهر فيها الربح ، وملك المضارب بعض الربح ، فنفذت دعوته فيها. ويجب عليه لرب المال رأس ماله، وهو ألف، ويجب عليه أيضاً نصيبه من الربح ، مائتان وخمسون درهماً ، فإذا وصل إلى يده ألف استوفى رأس المال، وصار الولد وهو كله ربحاً، فيملك المضارب منه نصفه فيعتق عليه، وما لم يصل إلى ربِّ المال الألف فالولد رقيق، ثم يأخذ منه مئتين وخمسين على أنه نصيبه من الربح. ولو ازدادت قيمتها عتق الولد، وصارت الجارية أمّ ولد له ؛ لأن الربح ظهر في كل واحد منها، ويأخذ رأس المال من المضارب وما بقي من نصيبه من الربح، ويضمن أيضاً نصف عقرها ؛ لأنه لما استوفى رأس المال ظهر أنه ربح ؛ لأنَّ عقر مال المضاربة يكون للمضاربة، ويسعى الغلامُ في نصيب ربِّ المال، ويسقط عنه نصيب المضارب. ذكره العيني، وغيره.
[1] His saying: 'goods (a'yan)' means different types in reality or legally. Even if the goods are of one type, each item equal to the capital, profit appears, as if he buys two horses each worth one thousand, and the capital is one thousand, he has one-fourth of them. Even if a man gives (one) as a gift and hands it over to him, it is valid. Profit does not appear; rather, each one is suitable to be the capital because it is possible that the other perishes and only one remains, so there is no preference for either as capital or profit. Then if the value increases after the claim until the child's value becomes one thousand five hundred, profit appears, the previous claim is executed, lineage is established, and the child is emancipated due to his ownership in part. As for the slave (male), according to Abu Hanifa, he has different types due to the great disparity in hidden meanings, and according to both (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) as well, unless the judge sees benefit in all, or they mutually agree, then they are combined. Thus in al-Kifayah. [1] His saying: 'Profit does not appear' – if profit does not appear, the mudarib has no ownership in the slave-girl, and without ownership, istila' (possession) is not established. [2] His saying: 'Then if the value increases...' – even if the child's value does not increase beyond one thousand, and the mother's value increases to one thousand five hundred, the slave-girl becomes umm walad for the mudarib, and he guarantees to the principal one thousand dirhams and two hundred fifty dirhams, because when her value increased, profit appeared in her, and the mudarib owned some profit, so his claim in her is executed. He owes the principal his capital, which is one thousand, and also his share of profit, two hundred fifty dirhams. So if one thousand reaches his hand, he has satisfied the capital, and the child becomes all profit, so the mudarib owns half of it and it is emancipated for him. As long as the one thousand has not reached the principal, the child remains a slave. Then he takes from him two hundred fifty as his share of profit. If her value increases further, the child is emancipated and the slave-girl becomes umm walad for him, because profit appears in each of them. He takes the capital from the mudarib and the remainder of his share of profit, and also guarantees half of her 'uqr (dower) because when he satisfied the capital, it becomes apparent that it is profit; because the 'uqr of mudarabah property belongs to the mudarabah. The boy seeks compensation for the principal's share, and the mudarib's share is dropped. Mentioned by al-'Ayni and others.
Source pages p. 369

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the ruling regarding a mudarib's claim of paternity and the role of profit. It begins by glossing the term 'a'yan' (specific goods) from the matn. The commentator explains that if the mudarabah capital is converted into goods that are all of different types (in reality or legally), profit is determined by comparing each item to the capital. If the goods are of one type, each item equal to the capital, profit is not immediately apparent because any one item could represent the capital if the others perish. For example, if the mudarib buys two horses each worth 1000 dirhams with a capital of 1000, he owns one-fourth of each (since the capital is half of the total value, but the mudarib's share of profit is half of the remaining after capital, so effectively one-fourth). If the mudarib gifts one horse, it is valid. However, profit is not realized until the total value exceeds the capital. The condition for the mudarib's claim of paternity to be effective is that profit must have appeared, giving him ownership in the slave-girl. If the child's value increases after the claim (e.g., to 1500), profit appears, the earlier claim is executed, lineage is established, and the child is emancipated proportionally to the mudarib's share. The passage then notes an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the classification of goods: according to Abu Hanifa, if the goods are of different types (e.g., a male slave), they are considered different due to significant disparity in hidden attributes, so the same rule applies. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), the same applies unless the judge sees overall benefit or the parties agree, in which case they can be combined (i.e., treated as one type). The commentary then provides further detail: if the child's value does not increase but the mother's value does (to 1500), the mother becomes umm walad for the mudarib. He must pay the principal 1250 dirhams (1000 capital + 250 profit share). Once the capital is paid, the child becomes entirely profit, half owned by the mudarib and freed, while the other half remains the principal's until paid. If values increase further, both child and mother are affected: the child is freed, the mother is umm walad, and the mudarib must pay the capital and his remaining profit share, plus half of the 'uqr (compensation for using the slave-girl) because after capital satisfaction, it is profit. The slave-boy then works to compensate the principal's share, and the mudarib's share is dropped. This is based on the principle that the 'uqr of mudarabah property belongs to the mudarabah itself. The commentator attributes this to al-'Ayni and others.

Key Terms
أعيان (a'yan): Specific, tangible goods purchased with mudarabah capital, as opposed to cash.
عقر (uqr): Compensation for using a slave-girl, typically paid to the owner for loss of value due to pregnancy or childbirth.
استيلاء (istila'): Legal possession or control, which is a prerequisite for a valid claim of paternity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, when does profit appear in a mudarabah involving goods?
A) Immediately upon purchase of goods.
B) Only after the goods are sold and cash in hand.
C) When the total value of all goods exceeds the capital.
D) When any single item's value exceeds its cost.

Key Takeaway
Profit in mudarabah goods appears only when total value exceeds capital, enabling the mudarib's ownership and claim.
